```
sensible sort of chap...If he is saying the same as I said (and he isn't,
but you have interpreted that he is...) then how come he doesn't get rapped
for being over the top?

> You are both right, and there are a lot of users already doing this, and
I'll
> put money on it, doing much of it in a grossly inefficient way, with a lot
of
> that knocking down and rebuilding you refer to.

The knocking down and building is simply part of the "Software Manufacturing
Process". It is not part of the daily running. Instead of "writing",
"testing", "debugging", "UAT", "go live", it is simply "build it until it
works properly". How can this be "grossly inefficient"? (More so than the
existing process, which gets repeated every time there is a need for
maintenance.) So I'll take your bet...please send the money to my favourite
charity, "Sunny Acres Home for Bewildered COBOL Programmers" <G>


> What's important here is not
> "us" (the technocrats)  and  "them" the users, but rather, and this was
the
> focus point where I started in EDP - the 'well being" of the corporation
for
> which "us" or "them" are providing the service.
>
"Them" can provide a better service than "us" IF they are empowered to do
so... Their knowledge is about the business, not the technology. As the
technology SHOULD be the servant of the business, they are better placed to
administer it than us. (Well, obviously, they aren't at the moment because
the technology is still too technical. I see this changing, and that's what
my post was about.)

> No doubt you'll respond that IT departments can be just as inefficient -
no
> doubt there are some - but that is the problem of the managers ABOVE the
IT
> department.

Nope. I don't accept that the process of a Business user interacting and
iterating with smart software is inefficient in the first place... And the
more they do it, the better they'll get at it...

Anyway, the inefficiency you perceive in the IT dept. is the responsbility
of the people in that department; nobody else. While it might be nice to
pass the buck "upstairs", it isn't honest to do so. Yes, there is an
argument that says that Senior Management are responsible for EVERYTHING,
but in that case, why have IT Management at all? IT is no different to any
other department in this regard, we are all responsible for the shape we are
in.


>Yes I like your idea of mixed teams achieving this through
> components. Like all businesses you need tecchies in the background; there
is
> always that minor technical specification that can throw a loop into the
design.
> How often here, do we see among ourselves, "How do I use "X" with "Y" to
do the
> following in COBOL ?".
>
I believe you may have missed the point here. The "mixed teams" work well
with TODAY's technology. And, yes, we DO need "techies in the background"
TODAY. That is changing. It is being driven by Market Forces that are far
beyond our own little concerns over careers and futures...and the staus quo
and the Language we know and love.

Software HAS to get smarter.

Users HAVE to get more directly involved.

Today it is done with "Wizards" (and most people here will have used one to
set up their Internet Connections, just as a simple example...) Millions of
users all over the World, with no concept of Dial Up Networking, are
creating DUN blocks to connect to their ISPs with NO technical knowledge.
Seven years ago this was a specialist job requiring knowledge of Hayes
command codes, modem concepts, line speeds, and Telecom technology.  I
remember spending hours on my own and other people's systems grappling with
"possibilities" and changing various ports, IRQs, and protocols until it
worked. Today, 5 minutes with a Wizard and you're in. The same trend will
extend into Corporate Applications, and Components are making it possible.

> IT Departments should be run on a budget to judge their cost effectiveness
to
> the organization. Take a large chunk of their activity away giving the
users
> components to substitute - exactly how do you measure that the Purchase
> Department, Accounts Payable, Receivables, Treasury, Inventory,
> Distribution/Transportation and the big boo-boo - Marketing - are working
> effectively and efficiently, (i.e. for the lowest dollar cost output). ?

You don't care, if the amount is 30% of what it was costing to run the IT
Department...

Simple arithmetic. Set up the new interactive Visual Environments for
software manufacturing in the above-mentioned departments (Cost estimated as
a one-time charge equivalent to, say, 25% of current IT budget). Invest in
training (say, 10% of current IT budget), phase in the new user developed
systems, phase out the old IT developed systems (there will be a lot of
"cross-over" here with much of the old systems being "mined" into reusable
Components that can be used to build the new systems. The costs for this
will have been absorbed during the preceding year as standard IT activity),
and once it is all running smoothly, cut the IT budget  to support a few
Network experts, some hardware support, and an outsourced maintenance
contract on the new development software. A saving of around 50% in the
first year.

You can juggle the figures all you like; within 2 years at the outside, you
have a positive ROI. The measurements you mention above are then OBE
(overtaken by events...<G>) and become irrelevant. The bottom line is that
an investment in smarter software pays dividends in a very short timeframe.

>You
> can't just give the end users a tool - it's effectiveness has to be
measured.
>
The question is HOW you measure its effectiveness. My argument is that if
the overall saving is demonstrable and
dramatic, no-one will really worry whether ACCOUNTS are doing a better job
of using it than MARKETING...

> You can take for granted, at this point in time, such technical tools will
not
> be included in the weightings for judging the effectiveness of Cost (not
Profit)
> Centres. Some five years down the road, some aspiring management
consultant is
> going to realize this has never been questioned before - now he writes a
book,
> makes a name for himself, and bucks - "Ineffective Organizations using
> Components Inefficiently" <G>

In your dreams...

Efficiency is only important if it costs you money. Organisations absorb
inefficiency in processses and procedures (not just computerised ones) every
day. The only time they seek to really improve these processes and
procedures is when things are tough and the bottom line is suffering.
(That's why good computer staff have done well historically during
recessions...). At this point the inertia and costs of changing the status
quo must be weighed against the cash benefit hopefully obtained.

If two like-goaled inefficent processes are compared, and one costs a
fraction of the other, the relative inefficiency is irrelevant.

Pete.
```

```
Good post, Joe (as usual <G>)

Comments below.

Pete.

Joseph Katnic <josephk@iinet.net.au> wrote in message
news:150220022110153939%josephk@iinet.net.au...
> In article <3c6bb628_5@Usenet.com>, Peter E. C. Dashwood
> <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
>
> > "Them" can provide a better service than "us" IF they are empowered to
do
> > so... Their knowledge is about the business, not the technology. As the
> > technology SHOULD be the servant of the business, they are better placed
to
> > administer it than us. (Well, obviously, they aren't at the moment
because
> > the technology is still too technical. I see this changing, and that's
what
> > my post was about.)
>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
No argument TODAY.

Tomorrow it will be different. Components are already being used to build
network connections. A time will come when it will be possible to specify
the processing you require on ONE ATM and then simply tell the development
system to duplicate it as often and wherever you require on the network. As
a new ATM is installed and recognised by the Network, the software you built
will be automatically attached to it.

The whole point of my post was that they won't NEED "the necessary knowledge
to do it" that is required to do it today, because the development system
will shield them from this.

If you like, it is a kind of "deskilling". The trend is already emerging in
Visual Developement Environments for Programmers (IDEs). If I build a GUI
application with PowerCOBOL, for example, I can treat all of the Windows
controls as components and simply drag and drop them where I want them. I
then provide code to handle the events they raise (well, the events I am
interested in...) in COBOL and I'm done. The point is that I never have to
interface with the Wndows API to Create a window and specify all the things
it needs, as I would have 6 years ago. I am "protected" from the lower
levels of the technology (much as COBOL Programmers are "protected" from
Assembler knowledge of the platform they are working on...).

> And as COBOL is the king of this type of thing, I'm not sure where your
> component applies to COBOL.
>
COBOL is a good language to build commercial components in, but it is NOT
the ONLY one. Don't be too sure about ANY language being King of ANY kind of
thing. The relevance of Source Code is diminishing. The BEST language for
the particular task at hand is becoming the goal, and even that is only
applicable to places where they see the need to develop their own code or
write their own components.(The cost of software development is just too
high for many companies to continue to carry it, especially if they don't
HAVE to. Enterprises that use components don't care what Source code they're
written in because they don't have to maintain them.)

A particular incident (back in the days when a million dollars was a lot of
money <G>) brought this home to me...An insurance company who will be
nameless, in a country that shall also be nameless (but it is sometimes
called the "lucky country" <G>), were making pots of money. They had an IT
department that had an annual budget around $20,000,000. (In fact, they were
a mainly COBOL [mainframe] shop...). In a Particular year there were
devastating floods and fires and the rate of claims rose sharply. Even with
their considerable resources they were getting pushed to pay the claims...
The directors had a meeting and started looking at places where savings
might be made. The IT budget did not escape their notice.

"Why are we paying 22 million a year for IT; we are an Insurance company?"

Within 3 weeks the entire IT department was sold to a combination of IBM and
some others for around 8 million (including the in-house developed software
and application systems!). The service was then leased back for an annual
fee of 6 million. The Insurance people got on with the business of Insurance
and happily outsourced the entire IT department.

Today, they don't need to outsource it as long as it is not technically
demanding for their users to use it. Component technology is making this
more viable. However, I agree that it isn't there YET.

> I agree that user interfaces to the system - where they interface to
> gather information for reporting purposes - would be better done via a
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Well, time will tell... watch what happens in the next 10 years. The
mysteries of transaction processing will be encapsulated into components,
just as the mysteries of Database access have been by bound controls. The
majority of developers using RDB don't even use ESQL any more. They simply
invoke the methods of a Component that provides the dynaset they want, and
is bound to the RDB. A few years ago this would have been unthinkable (and
personally, I don't use it - I did on a couple of occasions because I was
doubtful if it could work...it does. And it does so very effectively - I
still prefer to use ESQL because it allows me greater control (at least, I
have persuaded myself that it does <G>), but many new programmers can't be
bothered with it and the bound controls serve them well.) yet today many
applications are churned out using these controls. (In this context a
"Control" can be considered a GUI Component.)

As a programmer in today's world, knowing the "sweat" that is required at
the nuts and bolts level to implement good on-line systems, I can understand
how you would have the opinion you are expressing, Joe. My argument is
simply that the Market place will (and is) demanding more such systems.
Therefore the "manufacture" of them HAS to get easier. A logical
extrapolation from this is that eventually, the building of such software
will be deskilled to the point where a Business User will be able to do it.

Personally, since the time I started in this game (1965), I have always
wanted to see computing technology firmly in the hands of the User base. The
invention of the PC by IBM, although it nearly lost them the Company, was a
major breakthrough in getting hardware to the masses. Components and Web
Services are a major step towards getting the software to the people.

I welcome it.

Pete.

> --
> Regards,
> Joe.
```

```
> > is the future. COBOL without viable OO is a non-starter. The OO
languages
> > will thrive, the non-OO languages will die.
>
> But most of the CoBOL still being written - is about extending the past.
Of
> course, that doesn't mean it's going to die - modern railroads are doing a
> large business - extending the technology of the past.  And they adjusted
> quite nicely when we switched to components that could network between
> ships, trains, and trucks without unpacking.
>
Sadly Howard you are right about this. I'm not sure about the railroad
analogy but the extension of the past is right on the button for many COBOL
shops.

> I suspect most of the people who program in OO CoBOL already knew CoBOL
> before they switched.  I doubt if many (if any) non CoBOL shops went to
> CoBOL for their web and net work.   Maybe they should have - but who's
going
> to sell that to management?

Again, you are right. I for one, am prepared to sell this to Management, IN
CASES WHERE IT MAKES SENSE.

It makes sense to use OO COBOL in places where the general knowledge base is
COBOL and can thus be "leveraged" to bring programmers with existing
knowledge of the Business into the world of Web and Network.

It makes sense to use OO COBOL for new development, because OO is simply a
BETTER way of doing things and can decrease maintenance costs dramatically.

It makes sense to use OO COBOL to "mine" the existing Legacy code and
convert it to components for re-use of existing, working, debugged
functionality.

Under any or all of the above circumstances I would sell the use of OO COBOL
to existing Management. And I'd put my credibility on the line to make it
work.

The only major risk is the learning curve. This means staff for the pilot
projects need to be carefully selected. I'd be looking for bright,
enthusiastic people with a capacity to try new approaches and a burning
desire to learn. I accept that sometimes this is a tall order to fill. If I
couldn't fill it, I wouldn't do it. It is a CSF (Critical Success Factor) in
introducing OO COBOL successfully.


>  They read about Java on the network, not CoBOL.

Yes, they do. But both these tools have a place. You don't throw away your
chisels because you bought a plane...

The answer is not to seek to villify or denigrate Java, but to show what a
potent cocktail Java and COBOL together can be.


>   I work in a CoBOL shop - but that's batch mainframe CoBOL - our Unix
> machine and LAN don't have or use CoBOL anywhere.

And that is typically the way it is in many places. Introduce OO COBOL on
the mainframe and, once your programmers have got the hang of it, they could
move easily to using it on the Network. Of course, it appears that IBM are
not interested in providing support for it on the mainframe (they reflect
the perception of their customers) so the window of opportunity is closing
rapidly.

A picture is emerging of where COBOL will be used, and it is not a pretty
one. See my previous posts here...

Pete.
```

```
incredibly raise objections, get  marked as 'non players'

I can assure you I apparently have deeply wounded one very nice gentleman on J4.

buck in this game - not sit thoughtfully, pondering  which little alleyway COBOL
should next progress down. I was almost tempted to quote this the last time he and

Commons. "You have been sat in this place long enough. Begone from this House !".
```

```
Before people start sending emails to (flooding) either Tom Ross or Tom
Dunham, let me clarify what I sent (in a private email) to "stringer".

1) First and FOREMOST,  IBM is "fully" committed to COBOL on the OS/390 &
z/OS platforms (and all other platforms that I know of where they currently
provide COBOL compilers - with the possible exception of OS/2)

2) IBM currently provides two EXCELLENT vehicles for existing (mainframe)
customers to communicate "enhancement requests"

  A) SHARE (in the US) and GUIDE and/or SHARE in various other parts of the
world
  B) via the "REQUEST" process handled by IBM service

3)  If you are NOT currently a PAYING customer of IBM's, then it is
(probably) true that they will listen to their paying customers when setting
their priorities "more closely" than they will listen to you.  However, if
you can show them "in dollars and cents" what they might gain by a change in
direction, then they would listen to almost anyone.

    ***

Finally, my private email to "stringer" was intended to get (for him - per
his request) a specific address that he could write to *IF* he wanted to
provide SPECIFIC input to IBM on some "direction" issue concerning IBM and
COBOL.  If anyone has such a specific request, then I would be glad to
forward it on - and try and get an "appropriate" channel to send the input.
```


---

<a id="t-c93791f5e3"></a>
## Thread: parsing COBOL.... PERFORM ambiguity? — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Language features and syntax`](topics.md#syntax)_

### parsing COBOL.... PERFORM ambiguity?

- **From:** duylam@hotmail.com (Duy Lam)
- **Date:** 2002-02-05T20:57:19-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<d372b267.0202052057.45ee2e2e@posting.google.com>`

```
I'm trying to write lex/yacc files for COBOL and I'm getting some
reduce/reduce errors that I've traced to the PERFORM statement. Doing
some searching on this ng I found some messages that mentioned
something about the PERFORM construct being ambigiuous.... is this
true? If so, can someone maybe give an example of an ambiguous set of
statements? Or if anyone knows why I might be getting these
reduce/reduce errors (any ideas at all), that'd be great. (And btw, I
am by no means a COBOL expert... just casual language knowledge, hence
why I'm not too familiar with these finer details)

Duy Lam
```

#### ↳ Re: parsing COBOL.... PERFORM ambiguity?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-06T00:08:10-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a3qh8h$iu4$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<d372b267.0202052057.45ee2e2e@posting.google.com>`

```
As I recall the "usual" problem - it has to do with how far in advance you
need to "read" and/or what you need to "know".

Consider

  Perform ABC

This could be the start of something like

  Perform ABC
  Display "YES"

where "ABC" is the name of a procedure to be "performed"

       OR

it could be the start of something like

  Perform ABC times
     Display "YES"
  End-Perform

where "ABC" is the name of a variable telling how many times to perform the
"inline" routine.

    ***

Also consider the case of:

   Perform
      Continu
    Display "ABC"

The question is

A) Is "continu" a mis-spelling of CONTINUE - and this was intended to be an
inline PERFORM?
    or
B) Is "continu" the ACTUAL name of a paragraph/section that appears LATER in
the procedure division.

    ***
P.S.  As far as I know, there are NO cases where a "valid" (ANSI/ISO
conforming) source program is actually ambiguous for the PERFORM statement.
On the other hand, what you may need to know may not be something that a
"simple" lex/yacc will provide easily.
```

#### ↳ Re: parsing COBOL.... PERFORM ambiguity?

- **From:** "Silvain Piree" <s.piree@enneya.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-06T08:29:51+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a3qm2c$13oa$1@news.kabelfoon.nl>`
- **References:** `<d372b267.0202052057.45ee2e2e@posting.google.com>`

```

Duy,

the problem you are encountering is probably related to following:

    "PERFORM" paragraph_or_section_reference
    "PERFORM" data_reference "TIMES"

When yacc encounteres "PERFORM A IN B" it doesn't know
which rule it should apply: "paragraph_or_section_reference" or
"data_reference".

The problem is that yacc is not very well suited for building a
Cobol parser. I can assure you that the above problem is not
the only problem you will encounter.

Also, why are you building your own cobol parser? There are
several open source alternatives, and numerous commercial ones.

Silvain
www.refactive.com

"Duy Lam" <duylam@hotmail.com> wrote in message
news:d372b267.0202052057.45ee2e2e@posting.google.com...
> I'm trying to write lex/yacc files for COBOL and I'm getting some
> reduce/reduce errors that I've traced to the PERFORM statement. Doing
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> Duy Lam
```

#### ↳ Re: parsing COBOL.... PERFORM ambiguity?

- **From:** "Ira D. Baxter" <idbaxter@semdesigns.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-06T08:55:19-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c6141c3$1@giga.realtime.net>`
- **References:** `<d372b267.0202052057.45ee2e2e@posting.google.com>`

```
We use a full-context free parsing engine to handle COBOL
for our DMS Software Reengineering Toolkit.
(See http://www.semdesigns.com/Products/DMS/DMSToolkit.html).
This gives us an easy way to handle the apparant
unbounded lookahead needed to resolve paragraph ends
and nested IF statements.

I think your problems with PERFORM are probably caused
by YACC's limitation of one token lookahead.
(Because of our context-free parsing engine,
we don't even notice this kind of problem).
To make a COBOL parser with YACC, I think
you'll have to add some weird hack in the
lexer to provide with the lookahead information
that YACC will not.
```

```
Hi @ all!

I have some problem, I need an example for a stored procedure.
Here we have an IBM mainframe with OS390, a transaction should be started by
a stored procedure which will be "called" from a java program.

So we have the way --> Java --> stored procedure --> transaction -->
cobol-program
and a string of 20 bytes which will be checked by the cobol program, this
prg should give a return-code back to java.

Is it possible to do so?
I have never seen a stored procedure, so I need someone to show me an
example, what is so special about stored procedures?

please help me quick, 'cause I don't know it myself and I don't have the
time to search the whole internet, ...

Thanks in advance

Tim Cordsen
```

```
I think that it is possible to eliminate 'sensible' as one of your
attributes regardless as how you behold yourself.  It is not the results
that would be obvious, it is the context.  Your code is not in an
appropriate context and so its function, origin or purpose are not clear

context in this thread and/or it is appropriately labeled.

a response to the question or a sensibly labeled example.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Stored procedure

- **From:** "Warren Simmons" <warren.simmons@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T00:15:51+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.databases.ibm-db2,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<XME88.1879$9%6.250728@bgtnsc04-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<a3rgk8$d1n4@doiftp1.volkswagen.de> <a3ri9c$kr1$1@panix1.panix.com> <3C6387EA.441DEEEA@Azonic.co.nz>`

```
With this discussion, I'm thinking that there are more than one definitions
of
stored procedures. Some are knee jerk, like this one of mine.

We had a 650 RAM with tape doing some work at a mill. The RAM (drum)
was too small for all the code needed for the various transaction codes the
applicaltion had to handle.

Solution applied, I think of as a stored procedure.  They put the code for
the
transactions on the disks with the data, so they could read the program and
data into the available memory to execute it.

Now days, I'd called a stored procedure one where I found a way to say
hello without using a persons name I could not at the moment remember.
A Knee Jerk. I wish I'd see more definitions than name calling.

Warren Simmons
Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz> wrote in message
news:3C6387EA.441DEEEA@Azonic.co.nz...
> docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
> >
…[20 more quoted lines elided]…
> might be different.
```

```
Tim Cordsen wrote:
> 
> Hi @ all!
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

A stored Procedure looks just like a program; for me they are in COBOL,
the difference is the way they are compiled and the bind statements.

The advantage is the speed of processing - my Stored Procedures are
called by a web application; updating various tables in predetermined
and complex ways.

my DB2 application is on OS/390 V 2.6 - DB2 V5; using ColdFusion for the
Web Application portion.
```

#### ↳ Re: Stored procedure

- **From:** Frederico Fonseca <frederico_fonseca@eudoramail.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-07T23:14:27+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.databases.ibm-db2,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5c266ucu9psf29hfc5k117ta30gbdupr2v@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<a3rgk8$d1n4@doiftp1.volkswagen.de>`

```
On Wed, 6 Feb 2002 16:03:34 +0100, "Tim Cordsen" <tim.cordsen@web.de>
wrote:

>Hi @ all!
>
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Just as an example (and not working as it is made of some pieces I
have left in my computer (it had a nervous breakdown) !!!), here is
what a program calling a stored procedure would look like
(including the creation of the stored procedure it self)


FF


----------------------

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID.  DEMO.
       ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
       DATA DIVISION.
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
       
       01  LDA.
           03  LDA-V2RC              PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  FILLER                PIC X(10).
           03  LDA-RC                PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  FILLER                PIC X(50).
       
       01  CURSOR-1.
           03  CURS-V2RC             PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  CURS-TYPE             PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  CURS-ROWS-PROCESSED   PIC S9(9) COMP-4.
           03  CURS-OFFS             PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  CURS-FNC              PIC X.
           03  FILLER                PIC X.
           03  CURS-RC               PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  FILLER                PIC X(50).
       
       01  HOST-DATA-AREA            PIC X(512).
       01  ERR-RC                    PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
       01  MSGBUF                    PIC X(500).
       01  MSGBUF-L                  PIC S9(9) COMP-4.
       
       01  PART-UPDATE.
           03  DESCRIP               OCCURS 3 TIMES PIC X(20).
           03  PARTNOS               OCCURS 3 TIMES PIC S9(9) COMP-4.
       
       01  BND-VARS.
           03  DESCRIP-ALEN          OCCURS 3 TIMES PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  DESCRIP-RC            OCCURS 3 TIMES PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  PARTNO-ALEN           OCCURS 3 TIMES PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
           03  PARTNO-RC             OCCURS 3 TIMES PIC S9(4) COMP-4.
       
       01  DESCRIP-CS                PIC S9(9) VALUE  3 COMP-4.
       01  DESCRIP-MAX               PIC S9(9) VALUE  3 COMP-4.
       01  DESCRIP-PH                PIC X(5)  VALUE ":DESC".
       01  DESCRIP-PH-L              PIC S9(9) VALUE  5 COMP-4.
       01  DESCRIP-L                 PIC S9(9) VALUE 20 COMP-4.
       01  PARTNO-CS                 PIC S9(9) VALUE  3 COMP-4.
       01  PARTNO-MAX                PIC S9(9) VALUE  3 COMP-4.
       01  PARTNO-PH                 PIC X(6)  VALUE ":PARTS".
       01  PARTNO-PH-L               PIC S9(9) VALUE  6 COMP-4.
       01  USERNAME                  PIC X(33)
                 VALUE "scott/tiger".
       01  USERNAME-L                PIC S9(9) VALUE  31 COMP-4.
       01  PASSWORD                  PIC X(5)  VALUE "TIGER".
       01  PASSWORD-L                PIC S9(9) VALUE  5 COMP-4.
       01  CONN                      PIC S9(9) VALUE  0 COMP-4.
       01  CONN-L                    PIC S9(9) VALUE  0 COMP-4.
       01  CONN-MODE                 PIC S9(9) VALUE  0 COMP-4.
       01  VARCHAR2-TYPE             PIC S9(9) VALUE  1 COMP-4.
       01  INT-TYPE                  PIC S9(9) VALUE  3 COMP-4.
       01  DESCRIP-LEN               PIC S9(9) VALUE 20 COMP-4.
       01  INT-L                     PIC S9(9) VALUE  4 COMP-4.
       01  MAX-TABLE                 PIC S9(9) VALUE 20 COMP-4.
       01  ZERO-A                    PIC S9(9) VALUE  0 COMP-4.
       01  VERSION-7                 PIC S9(9) VALUE  2 COMP-4.
       01  MINUS-ONE                 PIC S9(9) VALUE -1 COMP-4.

       01  CREATE-PKG                PIC X(256) VALUE SPACES.
       01  CREATE-PKG-L              PIC S9(9) VALUE 256 COMP-4.
       01  CREATE-PKG-BODY           PIC X(256) VALUE SPACES.
       
      * PL/SQL anonymous block, calls update_parts 
       01  PLS-BLOCK                 PIC X(100) VALUE
           "BEGIN add_parts(3, :DESC, :PARTS); END;".
       01  PLS-BLOCK-L               PIC S9(9) VALUE 100 COMP-4.
       01  ORA-ERROR           PIC X.
       01  RET-ERROR           PIC S99999.
       
       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
       
       START-MAIN.
           STRING
           "CREATE PACKAGE update_parts AS "
           "TYPE pnt IS TABLE OF NUMBER "
           "INDEX BY BINARY_INTEGER; "
           "TYPE pdt IS TABLE OF CHAR(20) "
           "INDEX BY BINARY_INTEGER; "
           "PROCEDURE add_parts (n IN INTEGER, "
           "descr IN pdt, "
           "partno IN pnt); "
           "END update_parts; " DELIMITED BY SIZE
           INTO CREATE-PKG.

           STRING 
           "CREATE PACKAGE BODY update_parts AS "
           "PROCEDURE add_parts (n IN INTEGER, "
           "descr IN pdt, "
           "partno IN pnt); "
           "BEGIN "
           "FOR i IN 1..n LOOP "
           "INSERT INTO part_nos "
           "VALUES (partno(i), descr(i)); "
           "END LOOP; "
           "END; "
           "END update_parts;" DELIMITED BY SIZE
           INTO CREATE-PKG-BODY

      *  Connect to Oracle in non-blocking mode.
      *  HDA must be initialized to zeros before call to OLOG.
           MOVE LOW-VALUES TO HOST-DATA-AREA.
           CALL "olon" USING LDA USERNAME(1:USERNAME-L) USERNAME-L.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
              GO TO EXIT-STOP.
       
      *  Open the cursor. 
      *  Use parameters PASSWORD, etc. for unused parameters.
           CALL "OOPEN" USING CURSOR-1, LDA, PASSWORD, PASSWORD-L,
                        MINUS-ONE, PASSWORD, PASSWORD-L.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
              GO TO EXIT-STOP.
      *  Parse the drop table statement.
      *  The statement is executed by OPARSE because
      *  the DEFFLG parameter is zero.
           CALL "OPARSE" USING CURSOR-1, DROP-TBL, DROP-TBL-L, 
                           ZERO-A, VERSION-7.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0 AND NOT = 942
           GO TO EXIT-CLOSE.
       
      *  Parse as well as execute the create table statement.
           CALL "OPARSE" USING CURSOR-1, CREATE-TBL, CREATE-TBL-L,
                           ZERO-A, VERSION-7.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
           GO TO EXIT-CLOSE.
       
      *  Parse the PL/SQL block.
      *  The statement is executed by OPARSE because
      *  the DEFFLG parameter is zero.
       
           CALL "OPARSE" USING CURSOR-1, CREATE-PKG, CREATE-PKG-L,
                           ZERO-A, VERSION-7.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
           GO TO EXIT-CLOSE.
       
           CALL "OPARSE" USING CURSOR-1, CREATE-PKG-BODY,
CREATE-PKG-L,
                           ZERO-A, VERSION-7.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
           GO TO EXIT-CLOSE.
       
           CALL "OPARSE" USING CURSOR-1, PLS-BLOCK, PLS-BLOCK-L,
                           ZERO-A, VERSION-7.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
           GO TO EXIT-CLOSE.
       
      *  Execute the PL/SQL block, calling update_parts.
       
           CALL "OEXEC" USING CURSOR-1.
           IF RET-ERROR NOT = 0
           GO TO EXIT-CLOSE.
       
       EXIT-CLOSE.
           CALL "OCLOSE" USING CURSOR-1.
           CALL "OLOGOF" USING LDA.
       EXIT-STOP.
           STOP RUN.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Stored procedure

- **From:** Susan A Allen <susan.a.allen@boeing.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T19:12:53+00:00

- **Message-ID:** `<3C642335.5EF5942@boeing.com>`

```


Tim Cordsen wrote:
> 
> Just to explain my situation:
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> 
Stored procedures can be written in more then one application.  I assume
you wish yours to interface with a DB2 table and return information to
the invoking code (there are also Oracle stored procedures)

You will need to code the processing part, compile and bind it
You will need to add the stored procedure to the proper DB2 table with
all the input and output parms properly defined
You will need to GRANT execute permissions to the Stored procedure
You will need to code the calling code properly to send in the input
parms and read back the output parms

Reading the manuals will get you there; this is how I learned to do it,
and I want to let you know it was a long & painful process to carve my
way through the wilderness when other people knew how; but I did not
know who they were.

I would strongly recommend you find a programmer and a DBA who have
worked with Stored procedures.  You will need to learn SQL or find some
one who does and some one who has strong JAVA skills & some one who
understands ODBC drivers and connections; you may also need to enlist
the help of someone who understands the RACF or security groups for your
particular shop (for such things as passwords).

I wish you well this was a slow process for me

	Susan A
```

## Thread: FUJITSU 5.0 calling a .DLL — 16 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### FUJITSU 5.0 calling a .DLL

- **From:** tomnj9612@aol.com (TOM NJ9612)
- **Date:** 2002-02-06T21:43:47+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20020206164347.20792.00002058@mb-cg.aol.com>`

```
Hello all,

     We are using Fujitsu 5.0.  We need to link to a .DLL to get information
back into the program.  When it calls the DLL we get the following message :

JMP00151-U cannot call PGRM GET
code 0x485

     The DLL we got, was a third party DLL. The company gave us what to pass
it, but it never appears to make it there.  I am assuming that we have done
something wrong with the linking of it.  
     Any help would be greatly appreciated.

Thanks in advance.
```

#### ↳ Re: FUJITSU 5.0 calling a .DLL

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-07T11:08:35+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c62536f_7@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<20020206164347.20792.00002058@mb-cg.aol.com>`

```
This is caused by the called program not being found, or the parameters to
it being incompatible.

Ensure the dll is in the current directory or on the system path.

DON'T try and statically link to it. Call it dynamically.

Ensure the parameter list you give it is in the correct order that it
expects and DON'T use RETURNING in your call.

Just pass the result field in the list like any other parameter.

example:
...
01  the-get-program   pic x(15) value "GET".

call the-get-program
      using    parm-1
                  parm-2
                  GET-result
      on exception
                  ....whatever
end-call

If this .DLL is an activeX control make sure it is registered with RegSvr32.
In this case you shouldn't be calling it at all (you must INVOKE its
Methods) so I'll assume that it isn't.

If it still doesn't work, it is probably because the .DLL is expecting
parameters by Value rather than by Reference. Consult the vendor and find
out EXACTLY what it needs, of what type, in what order, and HOW they must be
passed.

I would advise using a Component, rather than a .DLL. These simply plug in
to your application and are invoked easily. (See ActiveX above.) If you
really MUST use a .dll, expect to have problems with parameter passing,
especially if it is from a vendor who doesn't use COBOL.

It is possible to call .DLLs from V5. I do it all the time. Don't lose
hope...<G>

Pete.
```

```
What command are you using? You don't normally
link called DLLs (that's why they're called
'Dynamic'). And, of course, the operating system
has to be able to find them at execute time, so
you'll need to specify the path (somewhere).

In PowerCOBOL it's

INVOKE POW-SELF 'CALLFORM' USING 'entryname'
'dllname'

example:

INVOKE POW-SELF 'CALLFORM' USING 'MYBEGIN'
'MYDLL.DLL'.
```

```
JerryMouse <invalid@invalid.net> wrote in message
news:I6w88.13263$6o2.766541@bin4.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com...
>
>
> Oh Yes it is.
> "In PowerCOBOL it's INVOKE...." an astonishingly
> true statement.

Oh No it ISN'T!

Power COBOL is Object Oriented and therefore must use INVOKE to activate
object methods. However to Call a .DLL you would still need to use CALL. It
is not the use of INVOKE that I questioned. It is the use of the CALLFORM
Method as a means to call a non PowerCOBOL .DLL.

While your statement may be true, it is not applicable to the case in point.


> If he has FJ COBOL V5, he has PowerCOBOL - he may
> not be USING PowerCOBOL (although I can't imagine
> why not).
>

There are many reasons why people use or don't use a product. I share your
appreciation of PowerCOBOL and have used it for developing GUI applications
and COM components for a number of years now (since Version 3 (16 bit), in
fact). Nevertheless, when I want to call a third party .DLL I don't (and
cannot) use INVOKE. The only exception to this would be if the .DLL was a
registered ActiveX control or was an OLE (COM) server. Paolo mentioned this
in his post.

INVOKE is used to activate Object Methods. CALL is used to activate
sub-programs and external programs. (.DLLs come in this latter category.)

There are a number of things you have wrong in this post (usually you are
pretty right, but on this occasion you are demonstrating a serious lack of
understanding).

I believe you are using PowerCOBOL and have never looked at OO programming
and principles. If you had, you would understand the subtle distinction
between the use of INVOKE and the use of CALL.This is not an expressed or
implied criticism. Many people use PowerCOBOL without knowing OO. One of the
big pluses of the product is that you CAN do this.

Your statement above that if he has V5 he has PowerCOBOL is also NOT
accurate. Power COBOL is provided only with the Professional and Enterprise
editions of the product.

> >
> > See the response I wrote to him.
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Well, Jerrymouse, maybe you should do a little more testing and a little
less "thinking..."<G>

Wrong again. The extension is not required when calling a .DLL

You would know this if you had ever actually done what you are offering
advice about.

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: FUJITSU 5.0 calling a .DLL

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T07:44:09+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C6381C9.84DA3E5F@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<20020206164347.20792.00002058@mb-cg.aol.com> <ixi88.911$6o2.93385@bin4.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com> <3c625a8d_1@Usenet.com> <I6w88.13263$6o2.766541@bin4.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
JerryMouse wrote:
> 
> If he has FJ COBOL V5, he has PowerCOBOL -

No. Wrong.  Fujitsu comes in three price levels.  The Standard edition
does not include PowerCobol, only the Professional and Enterprise do.

> he may
> not be USING PowerCOBOL (although I can't imagine
> why not).

Because:
    a) he doesn't have it
 or b) it is inappropriate to his needs
 or c) he doesn't want to be locked to a single
       vendor 
 or d) he doesn't want to ne locked to a single OS
 or e) he uses another GUI such as SP/2
 or f) he has existing code he is porting to FJ

On point b), not all programs are appropriate for Windows 'point and
click'.  Some may be Web CGI programs, others may have no on-going user
interface, being background service programs.

In fact one of my gripes with many web sites is that they attempt to
provide 'a really nice user interface' for things that should require
_no_ user interface at all.  In some cases it is necessary for a user to
read one screen (their local computer system) and type into a web
enquiry screen and then read the results to be typed into the computer
system.

Get a decent program-to-program interface and the user need not be
involved at all.

I am sure that someone else with imagination can think of many other
reasons for not using PowerCobol.
```

```
********************************************************************************
Hi,
         I am agree with Jerrymouse's view. Generally DLL are not
linked, it is loaded at runtime. I do not experience with Fujitsu but
on OS/390 I dynamically called DLL. For calling DLL from COBOL program
you have to compile and bind COBOL program with
'RENT,NOEXPORTALL,NODYNAM,DLL' options.
         You can statically link DLL with COBOL but it is not a good
programming practice.
         Hope this helps.
Regards.
shyam
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: FUJITSU 5.0 calling a .DLL

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T07:59:12+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C63854F.F67BA17B@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<20020206164347.20792.00002058@mb-cg.aol.com> <c02fd744.0202062306.295c111@posting.google.com>`

```
shyam nivas wrote:

>          I am agree with Jerrymouse's view. Generally DLL are not
> linked, it is loaded at runtime. I do not experience with Fujitsu but
> on OS/390 I dynamically called DLL. For calling DLL from COBOL program
> you have to compile and bind COBOL program with
> 'RENT,NOEXPORTALL,NODYNAM,DLL' options.

I am not sure that describing a _completely_ different system is at all
helpful and is likely to lead to more confusion.

> You can statically link DLL with COBOL but it is not a good
> programming practice.

With Fujitsu (in my limited experience with it) it may be that small
stub library routines (.LIB) are required to be linked into the program
to satify the call linkage, these may then cause the DLL to load when
the program starts and they invoke the actual .DLL routines when the
CALL is executed.

This avoids one problem with .DLLs where the CALL is to a routine in a
DLL of a completely different name to that of the routine, as is mostly
the case.

He is calling 'GET' but I doubt that he has a 'GET.DLL' to resolve to. 
By statically linking a 'AddOn.LIB' derived from 'AddOn.DLL' containing
a stub for the 'GET' routine then the linker can resolve the CALL _and_
at run-time it will be known which 'GET' to execute.
```

```
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>

I belive that you can code the COBOL side to force dynamic linkage by using
the CALL <data-name> syntax.  As for matching the actual Function within 
a DLL with multiple routines/entrypoints, This should be able to be resolved in
the 
Run-Time Environment setup area.

[CALLDLL]                     <- main program
@EnvSetWindow=UnUse
IconDLL=F3BIIconn.dll

[CALLDLL.ENTRY]           <- entry point control for dynamic library calls
SUBPROGRAM3=SUBDLL3.DLL      <- <called name>=<actual dll file name>
Entry1=CALLDLL
```

<a id="t-7553aa1e52"></a>
## Thread: Solved!: Use of SYSIPT in COBOL II under LE/VSE — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers)_

### Solved!: Use of SYSIPT in COBOL II under LE/VSE

- **From:** Frank Swarbrick <infocat@sprynet.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-06T18:32:03-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** bit.listserv.vse-l,comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C61D913.62A905A@sprynet.com>`

```
Thanks to Gary Hasler for helping us solve the problem of opening the
card reader as a 'file' with COBOL II under the LE/VSE runtime.  As I
thought, this was not a programming issue.  It turns out that the
assignment for the virtual card reader that is set at IPL was a 2501,
which is no longer a supported device.  For whatever reason it still
worked under the COBOL II runtime but not the LE/VSE runtime.

My systems programmer IPL'd this morning assigning it as a 3505 (I
think) and everything now works!

Thanks to everyone who tried to help on this matter.
```

---

### Job Control Language

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol

```
Hi,
    Can anyone tell me anything about job control language, in the context
of which is the most widely used, I briefly encountered MVS/JCL whilst
learning COBOL at college but the material on it didnt go too deep. Whose
job is it to program JCL statements? Can anybody recommend a good book, with
a couple of examples, on the subject.

Thanks for your help
Bloggs
```

#### ↳ Re: Job Control Language

- **From:** Alistair Maclean <alistair@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>
- **Date:** 2002-02-07T21:01:39+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ie0BVBAzsuY8EwsS@ld50macca.demon.co.uk>`
- **References:** `<xjB88.5742$H9.1121688@news1.cableinet.net>`

```
In article <xjB88.5742$H9.1121688@news1.cableinet.net>, Bloggs
<bloggs.barney@NOSPAMblueyonder.co.uk> writes
>Hi,
>    Can anyone tell me anything about job control language, in the context
>of which is the most widely used, I briefly encountered MVS/JCL whilst
>learning COBOL at college but the material on it didnt go too deep.
JCL is a set of directions to the operating system by which you can
control the system. Essentially, and briefly, JCL links programs (on
EXEC statements) to the following datasets (on DD statements). There is
something called JES (usually JES 2 or JES 3) which permit further
control via statements like /*JOBPARM L=10. 

> Whose
>job is it to program JCL statements? 
Mine, yours and ops analysts. In most shops where I have worked, I was
responsible for writing new and amended JCL for live (production)
systems. I was also responsible for writing all test JCL. Only in one
shop has an ops analyst stepped in and done the live production work for
new systems only. So learn it.

>Can anybody recommend a good book, with
>a couple of examples, on the subject.
Wiley do a good MVS/JCL book. Sorry I don't know the name of it.
However, other posts on this news group have mentioned other books in
recent weeks. The best JCL book, IMHO, is the JCL manual. It contains
examples, too.

>
>Thanks for your help
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Job Control Language

_(thread depth: 7)_

- **From:** Rick Overmaat <rover@none.nl>
- **Date:** 2002-02-11T03:41:20+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C672F50.97AE438@none.nl>`
- **References:** `<xjB88.5742$H9.1121688@news1.cableinet.net> <ie0BVBAzsuY8EwsS@ld50macca.demon.co.uk> <z9C88.6055$H9.1134479@news1.cableinet.net> <D2D88.6282$H9.1152316@news1.cableinet.net> <d5258c4e.0202080148.2e15ec7c@posting.google.com> <12321C967241E1B6.C7B712A35E1DB8C9.44DD456E88DE584A@lp.airnews.net> <hPv98.19217$H9.2447741@news1.cableinet.net>`

```
Hi Bloggs,

I was amused when I read your questions and the answers.
As an experienced and well taught COBOL programmer, I would like
to add some general outlines.

Job Control Language (JCL) is the script language that belongs to
the standard operating systems of IBM mainframe (nowadays OS/390).
A mainframe is a very powerful type of computer. Most of the COBOL
programs on planet earth will be found on IBM mainframe, I guess.

But there are others:
CL (Control Language) for IBM's OS/400, the operating system of the
AS/400;
DCL (Digital Control Language) for Open VMS, the operating system of
DEC VAX and its successor, the Alpha;
and probably some more.

What do they do?
Suppose that you made a COBOL program called INVOICING.
The input comes from a file called SALES and the output is a file
called INVOICES.
In the ENVIRONMENT DIVISION you coded:
SELECT IN-SALES ASSIGN TO SALES
SELECT OUT-INVOICE ASSIGN TO INVOICES
IN-SALES and OUT-INVOICE are the names you prefer to use in your COBOL
program. But the script "knows" them as SALES and INVOICES.
The script then looks a bit like this:
   make memory for file SALES
   make memory for file INVOICES
   run INVOICING using input SALES output INVOICES
The user will not run your program INVOICING, but the script.

Do I need to have knowledge of them as a programmer? Well, often
I have to. How do you get the knowledge? From books and from having
a good look at existing scripts in the systems which I maintain.
Also from colleagues.

You wrote that you only received a rather superficial COBOL course,
at college. Then don't worry. If once you have to work professionally
with COBOL, there will be many things to learn. Not only the script
language of the operating system, but also file handling and screen
handling as they work on that OS.

For the OS that we started with, IBM's mainframe, for example,
this means: the about 450 pages book by Lowe on JCL, additional
information about the many MVS utilities, two equally big books on
DB2 file handling, two equally big book on IMS file handling, about
one book on VSAM files including AMS, and two on CICS screen handling,
if possible with good courses on all of these items.

So just finish college, I would say, and leave the rest to future and
fate  ;-)

Bye,
Rick

Bloggs wrote:
> 
> Thanks everyone for your help, it is much appreciated.
…[49 more quoted lines elided]…
> Version: 6.0.323 / Virus Database: 180 - Release Date: 08/02/2002
```

```
Jeez. Connect to COBOL files? You mean a file that was
created by a COBOL program? What kind of file is it?
An ascii file? Use the text ODBC driver.

 There is no such thing as an ODBC for COBOL. But you can
write ODBC *IN* COBOL. It is lots of fun!

I really hope there's some packed decimal, and some zoned
decimal data in this file... just to keep it interesting. ;)
```

<a id="t-7c36b26f0c"></a>
## Thread: COBOL/370 to COBOL/390 — 4 msgs

### COBOL/370 to COBOL/390

- **From:** srini_1969@yahoo.com (Srinivasan Thiagarajan)
- **Date:** 2002-02-07T20:41:26-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<aad67a18.0202072041.26162e3c@posting.google.com>`

```
Hi,

We have a requirement to convert a COBOL/370 application to COBOL/390.
In the Migration cookbooks, we have step by step convertion from VS
COBOL II and OS/VS COBOL.

I went through the archives of this groups and found that OS/VS COBOL
and COBOL/370 are similar.

Shall I use the cookbook for converting OS/VS COBOL to COBOL/390 for
my migration from COBOL/370? Is there anything specific I need to take
care?

Regards
Srini
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL/370 to COBOL/390

- **From:** scomstock@aol.com (S Comstock)
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T12:40:37+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20020208074037.18444.00000166@mb-bh.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<aad67a18.0202072041.26162e3c@posting.google.com>`

```
Srini writes ...

>Hi,
>
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>and COBOL/370 are similar.

What????? Not at all!

The progression is normally:

OS/VS COBOL -> COBOL II -> COBOL/370 -> COBOL for MVS -> COBOL for OS/390 ->
Enterprise COBOL

The biggest jump is OS/VS COBOL -> COBOL II
Some shops went OS/VS COBOL -> COBOL/370
Or even OS/VS COBOL -> COBOL for MVS
Or, in at least one case, OS/VS COBOL -> COBOL for OS/390

These four jumps are relatively the same magnitude.


Now consider COBOL/370 -> COBOL for MVS -> COBOL for OS/390

these steps are easy, almost trivial (one issue: new reserved words that you
have been using for data items or paragraph names in earlier code; but not real
likely).

>
>Shall I use the cookbook for converting OS/VS COBOL to COBOL/390 for
>my migration from COBOL/370? Is there anything specific I need to take
>care?

If you are at COBOL/370 and converting to COBOL for OS/390, just recompile and
re-bind. Odds are there will be few, if any, problems. [I would recompile and
bind from the lowest level subroutines up.]


Hope this helps.

Kind regards,


Steve Comstock
Telephone: 303-393-8716
www.trainersfriend.com
email: steve@trainersfriend.com
256-B S. Monaco Parkway
Denver, CO 80224
USA
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL/370 to COBOL/390

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T10:40:59-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a40vd0$siu$1@slb3.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<aad67a18.0202072041.26162e3c@posting.google.com> <20020208074037.18444.00000166@mb-bh.aol.com>`

```
As Steve says, upgrading from IBM SAA AD/Cycle COBOL/370 code to IBM COBOL
for OS/390 & VM (or the even newer IBM Enterprise COBOL for OS/390 & z/OS)
is normally QUITE simple.  It is discussed in the current IBM Migration
Guide at:

 http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/IGY3MG00/4.5

There is ONE thing that *might* cause you some work.  If your existing
programs are compiled with the CMPR2 compiler option, this option is still
available with COBOL for OS/390 & VM - but goes away with Enterprise COBOL.
Therefore, you should study the migration requirements for this change.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL/370 to COBOL/390

- **From:** Steve Burns <"stephen.d.burns2<at>boeing.com">
- **Date:** 2002-02-08T16:07:05+00:00

- **Message-ID:** `<Gr823t.M0@news.boeing.com>`
- **References:** `<aad67a18.0202072041.26162e3c@posting.google.com>`

```
If you do end up with significant code changes and have thousands of
similar (but not exact) changes to make, check out
http://www.raincode.com   they have software that will help or they will
contract to make the changes for you.
```

```
 o Recorded new location of the FAQ

 o Added some new COBOL books (particularly those written or contributed to - by
frequent comp.lang.cobol submitters).
 o Added information about LegacyJ (PERCobol) and changed the company name from
"Synkronix" to "LegacyJ".

where available

CobCy

Windows/98, and Windows/2000.

 o Added (back) information on the Tiny-COBOL ('74 Standard) project
```

<a id="t-2af28a94f2"></a>
## Thread: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files — 17 msgs

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

- **From:** "Kevin Steely" <kgsteely@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-10T03:51:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<X6m98.3587$421.307621@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
I'm getting a S0C4 abend when I use concatenated files as input.  The abend
occurs after a few blocks in the second file (in the concatenation) have
been read and processed ... not as soon as the second file is first read.
The abend occurs on an attempted MOVE of the file's Data Record (AI-RECORD)
to a Working-Storage record (AW-RECORD).  Presumably AI-RECORD is
inaccessible.

I get this problem regardless of whether the input files are tape or DASD.

If I gener the two input files to one input file and run the program with
that file, I have no problem at all.  The job runs to normal completion.
But if I specify the two files as an input concatenation into my program, I
get the SOC4.

By experimentation I have found that if in the program I list this problem
file as the second file in my OPEN statement (of the form OPEN INPUT FILE1
FILE2 FILE3) I can handle concatenated input just fine.  But if I specify
this problem file as the first file in the OPEN statement, I always get the
SOC4 when I run with concatenated input.

This just started happening all of the sudden.  This program used to run
fine with concatenated input.  Now it's abending all the time.  I haven't
compiled/linked it for several months.  Nothing obvious has changed.

Does anyone have any thoughts on this?  Any suggestions for correcting this?
As I say, I can rearrange the order of the files specified in the OPEN
statement ... which seems to solve my problem ...  or which gets me around
my problem ... but I would like to know what is really going on.

Thanks!
```

#### ↳ Re: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

- **From:** yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama)
- **Date:** 2002-02-10T04:46:34+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20020209234634.00581.00000387@mb-fh.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<X6m98.3587$421.307621@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
>From: "Kevin Steely" kgsteely@worldnet.att.net 
>Date: 2/9/02 10:51 PM Eastern Standard Time

>By experimentation I have found that if in the program I list this problem
>file as the second file in my OPEN statement (of the form OPEN INPUT FILE1
>FILE2 FILE3) I can handle concatenated input just fine.  But if I specify
>this problem file as the first file in >the OPEN statement, I always get the
>SOC4 when I run with concatenated input.

Ordinarily a S0C4 indicates a runaway subscript where the table extends into
the procedure division, however your statement here makes me believe that your
files have different blocking factors.  When concatenating files the file with
the larger block size must be first in the concantination.  It is possible that
while this program hasn't been changed the programs that create your files have
been.

Check it out.

Eileen
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

```
Agree with Eileen...
When the file is first opened, the BLKSIZE of the file is used as the
basis of a GETMAIN to capture buffer storage.   If any subsequent
files have a larger BLKSIZE, then they would end up generating an
address exception.
```

```
That changed because of system determined blocksize.  It used to be true
that non sorts had to have the largest first but that went away. 
Syncsort used to force something between files so that it could handle
largest other than first.  Check the FD for FILE1 and make sure that it
has BLOCK 0.  Also check for differences in the SELECT statements.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

- **From:** "Clark F. Morris, Jr." <cfmtech@istar.ca>
- **Date:** 2002-02-10T23:08:34+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C66FD3B.1BB48ACA@istar.ca>`
- **References:** `<X6m98.3587$421.307621@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <20020209234634.00581.00000387@mb-fh.aol.com> <3C66F851.1CD514A3@ix.netcom.com>`

```
Coding BUFL=xxx isn't a good idea if your shop is planning to use the
Large Blocksize at some point in time.  For those using other platforms,
IBM up until recently restricted blocks to 32767 bytes or less on anly
standard file.  Up to 64Kb blocks have been used by some special
dump/restore programs.  A recent innovation has lifted this restriction
theoritically to 2Gb - 1 and maybe even higher.  I know they are using
up to 262Kb blocks.  For some reason not clear to me the 32Kb
restriction hasn't been lifted for ANSI/ISO labeled tape.
```

```
Note the following comments are for IBM OS390 / z/OS and COBOL II or
later in that environment.  In reviewing this thread, the vital elements
are the SELECT statements, the FD statements with record descriptions
and the JCL.  Although I would expect a data management abend or return
of a non-zero status code if status code checking were enabled for the
file if there was a conflict between the JCL block size and the actual
block size rather than a protection exception, wierder things have
happened.  For COBOL programs on input files the normal program
blocksize overrides JCL provided blocksize overrides data set label
provided blocksize has been changed to JCL provided blocksize overrides
data set label provided block size overrides program provided
blocksize.
```

```
Kevin,
  This (probably) won't solve your problem - but does use a "preferred"
method.  Change your FD from

> 000090        FD  AIREELTP
> 000091            BLOCK CONTAINS 0 RECORDS
> 000092            LABEL RECORDS ARE STANDARD
> 000093            RECORDING MODE IS V

to

 000090        FD  AIREELTP
 000091            BLOCK CONTAINS 0 RECORDS
 000092            LABEL RECORDS ARE STANDARD
 000093            Record Varying in Size from 1 to 2468
 000094            DATA RECORD IS AI-REELTP-RECORD.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

- **From:** Steve Thompson <sthompsonNOSPAM@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-15T17:55:53-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C6D91F9.50F15441@ix.netcom.com>`
- **References:** `<X6m98.3587$421.307621@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <a47h02$l68$1@slb4.atl.mindspring.net> <EhZ98.7372$421.620030@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
Kevin Steely wrote:
<snip>
> What are the advantages and disadvantages of tinkering with BUFL?  I have
> half a mind to go ahead and add a BUFL specification for AIREELTP, but I
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> size?
<snip>

Forgive me for dashing this quick answer. I've been out of
town at a client's site since Monday and I'm trying to catch
up on several things.

The BUFL and BLKSIZE are related, but not the same. The BUFL
must be => BLKSIZE and all it does is make sure that the
buffer areas acquired are the size specified with BUFL. This
is a very old work-around to problems from way way back in
OS/360 days.

The only problem with BUFL is, if you set it too high, then
you will get x buffers of that size that have to be paged.
However, when I/O is done, the whole buffer has to be page
fixed. Ok, let's look at it this way:  Absolute max buffer
size is 8192 but you specify BUFL=32000. Also assume that
your system will default to 5 buffers. So 5 buffers of 32000
must be obtained (and backed by real page frames!). But you
won't S0C4 on a buffer overflow because you now own the
storage beyond the actual buffer (8192?).

So the advantage is, if you are using NON-cataloged data
sets, then you can make sure that any READ will not cause a
block to be obtained that is longer than any buffer. The
disadvantage is, BUFL is static and not dynamic. So you will
use that buffer length (size) regardless of how big or small
the actual blocksize is.

I wish I had some more time to look/work on this with/for
you. But, I must take off to get things done and probably
won't be back to my tube until Monday.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

- **From:** "Clark F. Morris, Jr." <cfmtech@istar.ca>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T04:06:04+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C706F59.DD607631@istar.ca>`
- **References:** `<X6m98.3587$421.307621@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <a47h02$l68$1@slb4.atl.mindspring.net> <EhZ98.7372$421.620030@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
The light dawneth.  You have described the record as 2468 bytes long. 
If in fact it is less than that and it is the last record in the block
or the effective length of it plus the rest of the records in the block
is less than 2468 bytes, when you move it you are addressing memory
beyond the end of the block.  Depending on the size of the buffer, which
normally is the size of the block including block descriptor word and
probably rounded to a double word and how the GETMAIN was done, you will
be addressing memory not allocated to your program.  

Two solutions, both of which require that you add a RECORD VARYING
DEPENDING ON RECL-IN-WORKING-STORE-UNSIGNED clause where
RECL-IN-WORKING-STORE-UNSIGNED (or your name) is a 5 digit or larger
unsigned field, preferably USAGE BINARY in working storage.  The first
solution is to do a READ file-name INTO working-storage-record.  The
second solution is to always qualify the move of the record with
reference modification (1 : RECL-IN-WORKING-STORE-UNSIGNED).

If you don't like those solutions, your program will always have to
determine the length of the record read and confine its operations to
the area actually read.

Clark F. Morris, Jr. CFM Technical Programming Services, Inc. 

Kevin Steely wrote:
> 
> Folks,
…[135 more quoted lines elided]…
> USED DIR BLKS       ===>             KEYOFF     ===>
```

```
maximum size buffer.

:>DEPENDING ON RECL-IN-WORKING-STORE-UNSIGNED clause where

:>determine the length of the record read and confine its operations to
:>the area actually read.

The compiler should handle this.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: S0C4 abend with concatenated input files

- **From:** scolby1606@aol.com (SColby1606)
- **Date:** 2002-02-26T20:56:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20020226155603.08406.00000674@mb-fk.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<EhZ98.7372$421.620030@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net>`

```
You don't say whether or not it processes any records before it falls over. As
far as I can see there are two possibilities:

a) Your READ has failed

You don't seem to have any FILE-STATUS clauses, so how do you know if the READ
worked OK (or for that matter, the OPEN)? Suggest checking the FILE-STATUS
after every file opereation. On all files. If it's anything other than '00'
(OK) or '10' (EOF), then write out a message. It's also good practice to  do
your OPENs one at a time as it's easier to check which ones have worked (or
not).

b) You have read a short record as the last record of the block. Because your
MOVE is a separate statement, COBOL will try to move the full 2500-odd bytes to
working storage. If the record is only 175 bytes, you will get a protection
exception when COBOL tries to access the remaining bytes that are off the end
of the buffer. This explains why the BUFL fix works, as it forces the operating
system to get a bigger buffer than you really need, just so that you can avoid
tripping over the end. The best solution to this is to use READ INTO instead of
READ followed by MOVE. COBOL is smart enough to move only as many bytes as you
actually read from the input record in this instance, and so won't run off the
end of the buffer.

Hope this helps.

Steve
```
