## Thread: How to restore PDS member statistics — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### How to restore PDS member statistics

- **From:** Håkan Sjunnestrand <sjunnestrand@mac.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-11T11:28:41+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C679CD9.CEEE6BC@mac.com>`

```
I send a job from my PC to a IBM Mainframe. The job have two steps.
First a IEBGENER step that save data transfered from the PC in a PDS
member. The second job step is a start of a REXX procedure. When
IEBGENER save in the PDS member I don't get any PDS statistics - I
mostly want change date and user ID. How can I generate this
information, in the IEBGENER step or in the REXX procedure?

/Hï¿½kan
```

#### ↳ Re: How to restore PDS member statistics

- **Date:** 2002-02-11T07:03:40-05:00

```
Hï¿½kan Sjunnestrand wrote:
> 
> I send a job from my PC to a IBM Mainframe. The job have two steps.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> /Hï¿½kan

IEBGENER will not put out the "USER" part of the PDS
entries. Probably the easiest way for you to deal with this
is via REXX and calling ISPF routines. There are a few which
will allow you to "edit" the file you have loaded via
IEBGENER. By setting certain options, you will be able to
get the editor to put out the stats in such a way that it
appears that you were the one that did the edit.

If on the other hand, you would like to have some real fun,
you can get your REXX code to read the PDS directory and
UPDATE it with the stats. I suggest dumping a PDS directory
that has the stats already in it so that you can see what it
is you are after. Be sure to take a careful look at the I/O
manuals that spell out how a directory block is built.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Converting ISAM -> Oracle RDBMS

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Geert Borstlap" <geert.borstlap@anubex.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-12T17:30:52+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c694493$0$75149$ba620e4c@news.skynet.be>`
- **References:** `<64d83439.0202110954.24144a11@posting.google.com> <D_W98.37916$vL7.1151602730@newssvr12.news.prodigy.com> <64d83439.0202120218.301440e3@posting.google.com> <7f9a8.57596$Ig2.15772311@news1.elcjn1.sdca.home.com>`

```
> > > > Does anyone know a tool which convert ISAM files to Oracle RDBMS
?
> > We're using MicroFocus Cobol...
> > So, I prefer a tool iso manual work.
> > Does anyone know such a tool? Are there other solutions?
>
> Do you intend to access the Oracle tables as if they were ISAM files?
If so
> you should be aware of the performance hit you will suffer unless the
volume
> of data is small. If you don't re-engineer for Oracle (or any RDBMS)
you
> will
> find that your programs will take much longer to run.
>

Well there is such a tool. And the remark of Jude Robert is true,
performance could suffer (a number of READ NEXT's starting from the
beginning of the file equalises a full table scan), but this can be
solved by reading records from the Oracle table block by block. Then you
only read a limited number of records at a time.

About a year ago, we developed a tool for a number of banks in Luxemburg
and Switzerland that is doing this job. It's called the "genIO"
(generating IO-modules), and it converts automatically all
COBOL-programs containing ISAM file-IO to the same COBOL-programs but
with it's data stored in an Oracle RDBMS. It also generates the needed
Oracle-CTRL files to load the data in the
RDBMS.
We're doing migrations of legacy platforms towards modern technology,
and the "upgrade" of Index-sequential COBOL files to a Oracle tables
(and changing all infected sources automatically) is a spin-off project
leading it's own life now.

Of course we can't simply change every READ in a FETCH, a WRITE in an
INSERT, REWRITE -> UPDATE, ...   This would be too easy.

There are 3 mayor problems when moving from C-ISAM towards RDBMS.
1) A sequence of COBOL file actions (OPEN, START, READ NEXT, READ
PREVIOUS, WRITE, INSERT, CLOSE, ...) works differently in an RDBMS. You
can READ on the primary key, continue READing on an alternate key,
switch direction by a READ PREVIOUS, ... and the fun has just begon.
2) The datatypes available in Oracle is only a subset of all datatypes
available in COBOL.
3) An FD (File Description) in COBOL can be defined with levels (03, 05,
07, ...) and OCCURS (arrays) whereas Oracle can only use a flat buffer
whithout OCCURS.

All problems are solved in an IO-module. This IO-module (one per file,
so in Oracle terms one per table) ensures that we get the same data, as
you would get with the C-ISAM version. All COBOL-programs are parsed,
stored in a COBOL-tree and regenerated, and every FILE-statement (READ,
WRITE, OPEN, ...) is automatically changed into a CALL statement,
calling the appropriate IO-module.

Well, the work is done in 5 steps. (which means you run the "genIO"-tool
5 times)

Step 1) (optional) analyse all COBOL sources and count the numbers of
ISAM files used and the number of "file-IO statement" replacements that
needs to be done. This gives you an idea how much work you have if you
want to do it manually.
Step 2) generates the CREATE TABLE scripts.
Step 3) generates an IO-module per FD description (ISAM file)
Step 4a) (fast data migration): generates the Oracle-CTRL files per FD
description
Step 4b) (slow data migration): generates a small COBOL program that
reads the complete ISAM file and INSERT record per record in the RDBMS.
Step 5) replaces every file IO statement in your COBOL program, and
replace it by the appropriate CALL IO-module statement. These new
statements are doing functional exactly the same as the original ones.

Now you create the tables in Oracle, migrate the data, compile the
IO-modules (.pco -> .o), compile and link your final exe's (with the
generated IO-modules) and you are ready.
After these steps you have your old COBOL-application working exactly
the same, however the data is stored in an Oracle RDBMS now. No manual
work needs to be done.

Some optimisation which are built in:
1) renaming: It is possible to choose new names for your fields in the
Oracle table.
2) The IO-module can be generated for all keys (primary and alternate
keys) or for a certain key alone. This produces smaller object-code.
3) The IO-module can be generated in an optimalisation mode. When you
would read your complete file  in certain COBOL programs (in Oracle i.e
a full table scan) this would boost performance.


We got good results in production. There was no performance penalty to
be paid.

So, I think this is about the tool you'll need. I invite you to take a
look at our website, where more details are explained.
http://www.anubex.com  and push the "the migration Centre" button. Or
you can mail me if you want to know more.

Hope this info helps.
Geert
(This is already the second time in a week that this topic pops up.)
```

```
This is an unmoderated Newsgroup, Herwig. You can post ANYTHING in ANY
Language.

However, as it is echoed around the World, your chances of finding an answer
to your problem (assuming you are posting a problem) is greatly magnified by
using English.

(Simply because there is a much greater chance of finding someone who has
worked with similar software or has encountered your particular situation,
if you post in English. In many cases, this person's first Language may not
be English either...but English (or some form of it...) serves as the
"Lingua Franca" in the Modern World.

Furthermore, as German Students spend 9 years learning English and are
generally pretty fluent in it, does't it make sense to use it <G>?

I believe there ARE COBOL groups in German. Try searching in Google (use a
German phrase or keywords...)

Pete.
```

### MS Cobol 5.0 and CGI

- **From:** "Salvatore De Salve" <cobra82@libero.it>
- **Date:** 2002-02-12T08:10:32+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3feca20dab38a09665ac218b2c139eb8.69229@mygate.mailgate.org>`

```
Hi,

I need to write a cgi in MS Cobol 5.0, then I write this source:

 

IDENTIFICATION DIVISION. 
PROGRAM-ID. HELLO. 
AUTHOR. Cobra. 
SPECIAL-NAMES. 
DECIMAL-POINT IS COMMA. 

DATA DIVISION. 

PROCEDURE DIVISION. 
****************************************
Main-Line. 
DISPLAY "<HTML>". 
DISPLAY " <HEAD>". 
DISPLAY " <meta name='Author' content='Cobra82'>". 
DISPLAY " </HEAD>". 
DISPLAY " <BODY>". 
DISPLAY "   Hi from Cobraï¿½". 
DISPLAY " </BODY>". 
DISPLAY "</HTML>". 

End-Main-Line. 
Ex-Main-Line. 
STOP RUN. 
****************************************

this program run in a dos shell but if call it from an html page it
does'nt run!!!

There is someone that can help me???

Hi from Cobraï¿½
```

#### ↳ Re: MS Cobol 5.0 and CGI

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-13T02:38:53+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c69b4ef_3@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<3feca20dab38a09665ac218b2c139eb8.69229@mygate.mailgate.org>`

```
The STOP RUN will prevent the Server writing the necessary header to the
Client.

Replace it with an EXIT PROGRAM.

You will also need an HTTP Header with "content type: mime/text".

Finally, are you actually running it in a CGI Environment? Like, you have a
Server or Server Simulator available?

Pete.
```

```
thru all following code until it fell off the end of the source code.

Win-CGI, which is a file interface, rather than httpd style
stdin/stdout, but given what he is attempting a STOP RUN is appropriate.

If he had been using Fujitsu and its CGI library then you would have
been correct.
```

#### ↳ Re: MS Cobol 5.0 and CGI

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-13T07:09:20+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C6A1120.E289DEDC@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3feca20dab38a09665ac218b2c139eb8.69229@mygate.mailgate.org>`

```
Salvatore De Salve wrote:

> I need to write a cgi in MS Cobol 5.0, then I write this source:
 
It can work, but to get displays to go to 'stdout' you will need to have
an environment variable COBSW=S5
 
> IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
> PROGRAM-ID. HELLO.
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> does'nt run!!!

You are not putting out a content header which is a requirement.

         DISPLAY "Content-Type: text/html"
         DISPLAY " "

Whether this will work may depend on the web server you use.  Some will
not run DOS programs, some will uses files to interface (WIN-CGI).  MS
Cobol 5 will allow you to compile 16bit Windows and these will work with
Xitami server (www.xitami.com) on Windows.  To make it work as a Windows
program it does need some Windows API bits.

You can also use CobolScript (www.deskware.com) but this is not quite
the same as Cobol and won't, for example, read MS ISAM files.

I have quite large Cobol CGI programs using an equivalent to MS Cobol
4.5 and they run on Windows/Xitami, OS/2/Xitami, DOS/Windows3.1/(forget
the web server name) and recompile for Linux/Apache.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: MS Cobol 5.0 and CGI

##### ↳ ↳ It's WORKING :-)

- **From:** "Salvatore De Salve" <cobra82@libero.it>
- **Date:** 2002-02-13T20:11:08+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7082c499957189f060998137165676e3.69229@mygate.mailgate.org>`
- **References:** `<3feca20dab38a09665ac218b2c139eb8.69229@mygate.mailgate.org> <3C6A1120.E289DEDC@Azonic.co.nz>`

```
Hi
OKKKKKKKKKK!!!!!!!!!!

It's working fine!!! I've installed the xitami WEB server.
The final's source code is:

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID. HELLO.
       AUTHOR. Cobra.
       SPECIAL-NAMES.
           DECIMAL-POINT IS COMMA.

       DATA DIVISION.

       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
      *****************************************************
       Main-Line.
           DISPLAY "Content-type: text/html".
           DISPLAY " ".
           DISPLAY "<HTML>".
           DISPLAY "  <HEAD>".
           DISPLAY "    <TITLE>Prova CGI Cobol</TITLE>".
           DISPLAY "  </HEAD>".
           DISPLAY "  <BODY>".
           DISPLAY "    Ciao da Cobraï¿½".
           DISPLAY "  </BODY>".
           DISPLAY "</HTML>".

           STOP RUN.
      *****************************************************

and I've compiled the program with:
   cobol hello,,,,

and I've linked the objec's file:
   link hello+adis+adisinit+adiskey,,,lcobol+cobapi/nod;

I haven't add the "SET" variable  "COBSW=S5" because it preventing the
program run.

Thank's very much and excume for my english!!! ;-)

Cobraï¿½
```

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C6BFD27.EA9371F6@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<3feca20dab38a09665ac218b2c139eb8.69229@mygate.mailgate.org> <3C6A1120.E289DEDC@Azonic.co.nz> <a5619d1c173622ec86c7c6b630ee051d.69229@mygate.mailgate.org>`

```
Salvatore De Salve wrote:
> 
> Ok, and now how I can get:
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> Thank's so much.

Yes, I thought that may be next on the list.

You need to get the environment variables that the Web Server sets:

     01  CGI-Environment-Names.
      03 N-Query-String      PIC X(20) VALUE "QUERY_STRING".
      03 N-Auth-Type         PIC X(20) VALUE "AUTH_TYPE".
      03 N-Content-Encoding  PIC X(20) VALUE "CONTENT_ENCODING".
      03 N-Content-Length    PIC X(20) VALUE "CONTENT_LENGTH".
      03 N-Content-Type      PIC X(20) VALUE "CONTENT_TYPE".
      03 N-GateWay-Interface PIC X(20) VALUE "GATEWAY_INTERFACE".
      03 N-HTTP-Accept       PIC X(20) VALUE "HTTP_ACCEPT".
      03 N-HTTP-Cookie       PIC X(20) VALUE "HTTP_COOKIE".
      03 N-HTTP-User-Agent   PIC X(20) VALUE "HTTP_USER_AGENT".
      03 N-Path-Info         PIC X(20) VALUE "PATH_INFO".
      03 N-Path-Translated   PIC X(20) VALUE "PATH_TRANSLATED".
      03 N-Referer-URL       PIC X(20) VALUE "REFERER_URL".
      03 N-Remote-Addr       PIC X(20) VALUE "REMOTE_ADDR".
      03 N-Remote-Host       PIC X(20) VALUE "REMOTE_HOST".
      03 N-Remote-User       PIC X(20) VALUE "REMOTE_USER".
      03 N-Request-Method    PIC X(20) VALUE "REQUEST_METHOD".
      03 N-Server-Name       PIC X(20) VALUE "SERVER_NAME".
      03 N-Server-Port       PIC X(20) VALUE "SERVER_PORT".
      03 N-Server-Protocol   PIC X(20) VALUE "SERVER_PROTOCOL".
      03 N-Server-Software   PIC X(20) VALUE "SERVER_SOFTWARE".
      03 N-End               PIC X(20) VALUE SPACES.

     01  CGI-N-RDF REDEFINES CGI-Environment-Names.
      03 N-Environment-Name  PIC X(20) OCCURS 21.

     01  CGI-Windows-Names.
      03 W-Query-String      PIC X(20) VALUE "Query String".
      03 W-Auth-Type         PIC X(20) VALUE "AUTH_TYPE".
      03 W-Content-Encoding  PIC X(20) VALUE "Content File".
      03 W-Content-Length    PIC X(20) VALUE "Content Length".
      03 W-Content-Type      PIC X(20) VALUE "Content Type".
      03 W-GateWay-Interface PIC X(20) VALUE "GATEWAY_INTERFACE".
      03 W-HTTP-Accept       PIC X(20) VALUE "Accept".
      03 W-HTTP-Cookie       PIC X(20) VALUE "HTTP_COOKIE".
      03 W-HTTP-User-Agent   PIC X(20) VALUE "HTTP_USER_AGENT".
      03 W-Path-Info         PIC X(20) VALUE "PATH_INFO".
      03 W-Path-Translated   PIC X(20) VALUE "PATH_TRANSLATED".
      03 W-Referer-URL       PIC X(20) VALUE "REFERER_URL".
      03 W-Remote-Addr       PIC X(20) VALUE "Remote Address".
      03 W-Remote-Host       PIC X(20) VALUE "Remote Host".
      03 W-Remote-User       PIC X(20) VALUE "Remote User".
      03 W-Request-Method    PIC X(20) VALUE "Request Method".
      03 W-Server-Name       PIC X(20) VALUE "Server Name".
      03 W-Server-Port       PIC X(20) VALUE "Server Port".
      03 W-Server-Protocol   PIC X(20) VALUE "SERVER_PROTOCOL".
      03 W-Server-Software   PIC X(20) VALUE "Server Software".
      03 W-End               PIC X(20) VALUE SPACES.

     01  CGI-W-RDF REDEFINES CGI-Windows-Names.
      03 W-Environment-Name  PIC X(20) OCCURS 21.

These can be accessed using DISPLAY name UPON ENVIRONMENT-NAME, ACCEPT
value FROM ENVIRONMENT-VALUE, or by using CALL "_EXTNAME" in MS/MF
Cobol.

CGIINPUT.CBL program (old version) attached will help (if attachment
works).  Processing the URL query string requires converting '+' to
space, '%nn' to character x"nn" and breaking up the string on &s.
```

## Thread: CobAnal — 1 msgs

### CobAnal

- **From:** "Roland Schiradin" <schiradi@tap.de>
- **Date:** 2002-02-12T22:11:59+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4ehqf$8md$1@wrath.news.nacamar.de>`

```
OS/390,MVS, z/OS user  FYI

The newest version of CobAnal is available at http://www.cbttape.org
FILE321 (Select Updates)

This version supports now the newest Cobol from IBM Cobol Enterprise V3R1
and add support for wildcards.

CobAnal analyze a given loadlib and report all Cobol programs (every
version) and
display a lot of infortmation you may never seen before.

A real nice ISPF interface can be found in FILE330

Regards Roland
```

```
Sorry if I was in any way offensive. But - as a mainframe programmer - I've
used MicroFocus Cobol & Mainframe Express - and MFE wins hands down every
time, in pretty much every category. However, I said "pretty much every
category" as I'm sure some Pedant will correct me.

MFE offers a full GUI interface, matches MF in most categories except in
volume testing, where it leaves the DB's on the mainframe, and runs  the job
remotely. I loved this product, and would have continued to use it - ahead
of the mainframe & BTS/Expediter/Intertest batch enivronment, except my
client (an international credit card company - #3 in the world) decided not
to buy one of the versions of Release 2.

I should have been thankful for small mercies - my current client is a state
Dept. of Transportation, that won't pay $30 for a shareware product that
does a source file compare- thank G*D for SUPERC (which is better anyway) !
```

#### ↳ Re: REQUEST: PLEASE POST ** MICRO FOCUS COBOL *** THANK YOU !!!!!

- **From:** thaneh@softwaresimple.com (Thane Hubbell)

```
What does this mean?
```

```
> "Markus Grossmann" <markus@remove-grossm.de> wrote in message
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
> clause


If you can't find a compiler option which supports supports REDEFINES of
ODO, recoding this is easy enough....

01 TLINE.
  05  TLINES  PIC X(79).
  05 FILLER REDEDFINES TLINES.
      10 TLINER    PIC X(01) OCCURS 79 DEPENDING ON SUB5.

I think if you can get the ODO as the last data name of the group item (the
01) you should be OK with just about any compiler.

MCM
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Markus Grossmann" <markus@remove-grossm.de>
- **Date:** 2002-02-13T17:47:33+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<AMwa8.8592$%5.1540574236@news.tli.de>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <a4e0le$l02$1@slb5.atl.mindspring.net> <EKva8.8591$Ke3.1540293761@news.tli.de> <a4e2d6$uvf$1@slb4.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
ODOOSVS
...Makes the evaluation of OCCURS DEPENDING ON items more compatible with
the OS/VS COBOL compiler.

When ODOOSVS is specified, the length of variable-length groups and the
address of items following variable-length tables is evaluated at the time
when the OCCURS DEPENDING ON item is modified, rather than at the time when
the variable-length group or sliding data item is referenced.


Tested with -C NOODOOSVS didn't make any change. Sorry.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

- **From:** Harald.Cordes@microfocus.com (Harald Cordes)
- **Date:** 2002-02-14T08:43:48-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1fabdc0d.0202140843.11769aff@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <3C6AA6DA.AC2A158F@shaw.ca> <FQKa8.8606$IO1.1545609329@news.tli.de>`

```
Please code as:
       01 TLINER OCCURS 79 DEPENDING ON SUB5 PIC X VALUE SPACE.
       01 TLINES REDEFINES TLINER           PIC X(79).

A redefinition of an ODO is not allowed in ANSI 85 and was disallowed
for other than 01 levels some versions ago in MF, because a
       move all "A" to TLINE *> 01 TLINE ...
is ambiguous, if SUB5 is not equal to 79.

Some older versions of MF COBOL erroneously allowed this.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "ronald leenheer" <r.leenheer@wanadoo.nl>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T00:15:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bIXb8.14$Qn1.281@castor.casema.net>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <3C6AA6DA.AC2A158F@shaw.ca> <FQKa8.8606$IO1.1545609329@news.tli.de> <1fabdc0d.0202140843.11769aff@posting.google.com>`

```
No Occurs at level 01!!!
The rule is Value/Redefines/Occurs

Should be:
01  TLINE.
      03   TLINER-GROUP        VALUE SPACE.
             05 TLINER OCCURS 79 DEPENDING ON SUB5 PIC X.
      03 TLINES REDEFINES TLINER-GROUP                 PIC X(79).

Ronald Leenheer

"Harald Cordes" <Harald.Cordes@microfocus.com> schreef in bericht
news:1fabdc0d.0202140843.11769aff@posting.google.com...
> Please code as:
>        01 TLINER OCCURS 79 DEPENDING ON SUB5 PIC X VALUE SPACE.
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> Some older versions of MF COBOL erroneously allowed this.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T18:45:47+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c70979b_1@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <3C6AA6DA.AC2A158F@shaw.ca> <FQKa8.8606$IO1.1545609329@news.tli.de> <1fabdc0d.0202140843.11769aff@posting.google.com> <bIXb8.14$Qn1.281@castor.casema.net>`

```

ronald leenheer <r.leenheer@wanadoo.nl> wrote in message
news:bIXb8.14$Qn1.281@castor.casema.net...
> No Occurs at level 01!!!
> The rule is Value/Redefines/Occurs
>
Yes, Ronald, that is indeed the rule if you want REDEFINES and OCCURS to
play nicely together...(It isn't quite that rigid and can be broken as long
as you know exactly what you are doing, but it is a VERY GOOD rule for
people new to COBOL to remember...)

So why did you break it with the sample you posted below, where you have
Value/Occurs/Redefines <G>?
(And you haven't done the things you would need to do to make this work...).

It is hardly helpful to offer a rule, then immediately give an example that
violates it, is it?

Try this...

01  tline.
      12 tline-group pic x(79) value space.
      12 varlen-tline redefines tline-group.
           15 vtline-char pic x  occurs 79
                                          depending on sub-5.

It should be pointed out that this is a completely pointless exercise.
Nothing will be gained by using OCCURS...DEPENDING ON (ODO). If you really
want to pick up chunks of tline that vary in size up to 79 bytes, and given
that the required length has been set into sub-5, then use Reference
Modification. This avoids the use of ODO altogether and gives a much better
result...

01  tline      pic x(79) value space.
...
move 12 to sub-5
move tline (1:sub-5) to ...

this will move 12 characters from the start of tline to wherever you want.
Setting any value, up to 79, in sub-5 before the move will do likewise.

If your requirement is to do something with EACH CHARACTER, limited by the
number in sub-5, then:

perform varying
     J from 1
          by  1
        until  J > sub-5
             if tline (J:1) is interesting...
                ...do something with this character...
             end-if
end-perform

As you can see it is not ALWAYS necessary to use OCCURS and REDEFINES (never
mind ODO) at ALL, in order to get at varying data chunks. Sometimes in fact,
it is better NOT to...

Pete.


> Should be:
> 01  TLINE.
…[19 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

```
I am a "little confused" about what you are REALLY trying to do.  (I know
that you have existing code and you would like to make as few source changes
as possible - but lets think about what you want your source to do.)

Consider:

        01  peter.
            12 peter-group pic x(79) value space.
            12 varlen-peter redefines peter-group.
               15 peter-char pic x  occurs 79
                                        depending on sub5.

It looks (to me) as if you want "peter-group" to be a field that include ALL
79 occurrences of varlen-peter. If that is what you really want, they why
use ANY redefines.  Don't you get it if you have:

        01  peter.
            12 varlen-peter.
               15 peter-char pic x  occurs 79
                                        depending on sub5.

Similarly, why use

        01  ronald.
            03 ronald-group value space.
               05 ronaldr occurs 79 depending on sub5 pic x.
            03 ronalds redefines ronald-group  pic x(79).

instead of  (using ronald-group - instead of ronalds)

        01  ronald.
            03 ronald-group value space.
               05 ronaldr occurs 79 depending on sub5 pic x.


Now, the example

        01 haraldr occurs 79 depending on sub5 pic x value space.
        01 haralds redefines haraldr pic x(79).

Does something "quite different".  It seems to use haralds to redefine a
SINGLE occurrence of haraldr -= but that is redefining a PIC X field by a
PIC X(79) field which is always a "no-no" - and, as other have already
stated, using an OCCURS clause at the 01-level, is a REALLY bad thing to do
(and when allowed is an extension - with some very strange rules)
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

- **From:** "JT" <JTHK_17@yahoo.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-19T11:21:43+08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4sgah$8hn$1@news.hk.linkage.net>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <E99c8.8683$ip2.1574102069@news.tli.de>`

```
Hi Markus,

With regards to your program, there seems to be a bit of problem in your
definition of working storage items.  As far as I know, OCCURs DEPENDING ON
clause are used for defining variable length tables and in your sample
program, redefining a fixed length working storage item with a
variable-length table is wrong or are not allowed by cobol.  Likewise,
OCCURS on 01 level are always ignored or are not allowed by Cobol compilers
(I'm saying this based on my Cobol experience on mainframe).

More proper way of working around with it would be
01  SUB5            PIC 99.
01  WS-FIX-ITEM     PIC X(79).
01  WS-VAR-ITEM.
    05  WS-VAR-ITEM-FIELD  OCCURS 1 TO 79  DEPENDING ON SUB5  PIC X(1).
01  PETER.
    12 PETER-GROUP        PIC X(79)  VALUE  SPACE.
    12 VARLEN-PETER       REDEFINES  PETER-GROUP.
       15 peter-char      PIC X      OCCURS 79.


Regards, Jon.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-20T11:22:16+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c72d3d4_2@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <E99c8.8683$ip2.1574102069@news.tli.de>`

```
Markus,

your efforts are commendable and it would be good if more people posting
here did some testing and trying as you have done...

Your post raises several points:

1. Is what you are trying to do worthwhile?
I have discussed elsewhere in this thread that I believe ODO is the wrong
tool for this and Reference Modification would be better. However, given
that you have no choice, or it is an exercise for a course, then we should
really run it to ground and see what is going on.

2. Although COBOL is supposedly "standard" different implementations behave
differently.

Some vendors will implement the standard exactly, others will bend it to
make their product more "forgiving", others again will simply add extensions
of their own to it and encourage their users to stay with them.

All of this is highly debatable and there are pros and cons for all these
viewpoints.

Personally, over several decades, working with many different
implementations of COBOL, I have come to use a set of constructs that I know
will work across most platforms. I also avoid things that are likely to be
troublesome. I would NEVER use OCCURS...DEPENDING...ON of my own volition
because it is a stupid construct that achieves nothing. COBOL allocates
storage for the maximum size anyway, so nothing is gained. The only time I
have EVER coded this is because I was maintaining someone else's code and/or
a file definition used it.

3. Sometimes tutors put material in their courses which is interesting from
an academic point of view, but of very little use in the real world. I
believe this is  a sadistic streak in certain teachers and they enjoy
torturing students...<G> (e.g. I was helping a mathematics tutor earlier
this week with some programming stuff and she told me of a course at the
Polytech where she works, that makes students do arithmetic in binary, hex,
and octal, using fractions and WITHOUT Calculators... This is  a case where
the letter of the Law is more important to the tutor than getting a concept
to the class. I believe that ODO comes in this category and I would mention
it in passing but NEVER set exercises based on it or encourage its use in
any way...)

Having said all of the above, I was troubled  by the fact that the code you
were given by myself and others here, failed to work.

So I took your code and built a project with it in Fujitsu COBOL Version
6.1...

000010 identification division.
000020 program-id. test-odo.
000030 date-written. 02/02/18.
000040 environment division.
000050 data division.
000060 working-storage section.
000070 01  sub5 pic 99.
000080 01  peter.
000090     12 peter-group pic x(79) value space.
000100     12 varlen-peter redefines peter-group.

odotest.cob JMN2875I-W REDEFINING ITEM CONTAINS VARIABLE OCCURRENCE
 DATA ITEM. REDEFINES CLAUSE IS ASSUMED VALID.


000110        15 peter-char pic x  occurs 79
000120                                 depending on sub5.
000130 01  billK.
000140     12 billk-group.
000150        15 billk-char  pic x
000160                       occurs 79 depending on sub5.
000170
000180 01  ronald.
000190     03 ronald-group value space.
000200        05 ronaldr occurs 79 depending on sub5 pic x.
000210     03 ronalds redefines ronald-group  pic x(79).

odotest.cob JMN2874I-W ITEM REDEFINED BY REDEFINES CLAUSE IS
VARIABLE-LENGTH ITEM. REDEFINES CLAUSE IS ASSUMED VALID.

000220
000230* 01 haraldr occurs 79 depending on sub5 pic x value space.
000240* 01 haralds redefines haraldr pic x(79).
000250
000260 01 michael.
000270     05 michaels  pic x(79).
000280     05 filler redefines michaels.

odotest.cob JMN2875I-W REDEFINING ITEM CONTAINS VARIABLE OCCURRENCE
 DATA ITEM. REDEFINES CLAUSE IS ASSUMED VALID.

000290       10 michaelr pic x(01) occurs 79 depending on sub5.
000300
000310 procedure division.
000320     stop run.

I have placed the resulting diagnostics into the text above (Fujitsu
produces them in a separate window with a hot link on each one, back to your
 source code...)

I commented out the effort from Harald which was the only one that was plain
wrong and raised a serious error due to the occurs at an 01 level. This is
always a no-no...

As you can see the efforts from Michael, Bill Klein (although Bill dodged
the issue by avoiding REDEFINES altogether...a sensible approach but not
helpful in this case <G>), Ronald, and myself, all produced code which
Fujitsu considers OK. The diagnostics above are purely Informational
Warnings (JMN2875<I>-<W> f'rinstance...) and the code will run fine.

So you are left to draw your own conclusions.

Pete.
```

```
Russell Styles wrote:

>
>     I don't know how portable this would be, but on microfocus,
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> a small part of it.  Just be carefull.

You are sometimes left wondering when vendor extensions should become the norm;
sometimes their application seems so logical you wonder why a committee balks.

Case in point is the ODOSLIDE. Looks like the upcoming thing in OO languages
will be TUPLES and SPACE TUPLES, (check out IBM/Java sites) and these require
arrays/tables. Certainly I've seen somebody in an Eiffel group bemoan the fact
that that he can't easily get a variable array. And yet given that ODOSLIDE
directive in COBOL it is perfectly possible to create a collection with a
variable number of elements and a variable number of value fields per element,
plus the elements can be n-dimensional..

Jimmy, Calgary AB
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

_(thread depth: 5)_

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-21T15:39:43+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c745e80_6@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <E99c8.8683$ip2.1574102069@news.tli.de> <3c72d3d4_2@Usenet.com> <_sGc8.897$Im1.56838@bgtnsc05-news.ops.worldnet.att.net> <3C743ADB.5D1576CF@shaw.ca>`

```

James J. Gavan <jjgavan@shaw.ca> wrote in message
news:3C743ADB.5D1576CF@shaw.ca...
>
> You are sometimes left wondering when vendor extensions should become the
norm;
> sometimes their application seems so logical you wonder why a committee
balks.
>
That's why people ignore the committee and vote with their feet...<G>

My support of vendors for seeking to improve COBOL, DESPITE the
pontifications and machinations of the Standards body, is a matter of
record. Thank God they do it or we wouldn't have a Language.

> Case in point is the ODOSLIDE. Looks like the upcoming thing in OO
languages
> will be TUPLES and SPACE TUPLES, (check out IBM/Java sites) and these
require
> arrays/tables. Certainly I've seen somebody in an Eiffel group bemoan the
fact
> that that he can't easily get a variable array.

Collections do not REQUIRE arrays or tables. TUPLEs are instances of a
relationship, which is often implemented as a row in a Relational database,
or an element of a linked list. Usually the tuple consists of a key (showing
its position in an ordered set) and some related data. That's why they are
often implemented as rows (Relations) on an RDB. Tuples are not new, they've
always been a part of the Computer Science terminology for OO Collections.
The sets to which they belong can have an indefinite number of
"occurrences". (And, in my opinion, they should.)

The newly emerging Languages for parallell computing (like LINDA) are doing
interesting things with tuples like allowing asynchronous access to the
Collection.

The concept of using OCCURS is archaic and there is no need to limit systems
because of a COBOL construct. You know as well anyone here, Jimmy, that
collections can serve the same purpose as tables, with the advantage that
they are unlimited and dynamic and can have elements added, deleted, and
changed easily and freely, using the methods inherent in the collection. The
OO Concept of a collection is a more than adequate replacement for the
concept of a Table defined to a specific limit with an OCCURS cause. It is
the constant changing of these table limits that introduces errors into
programs and is the instigator for a large percentage of maintenance. If we
didn't have tables in memory, there would be no need to change them...

While I do not wish to denigrate Eiffel (I managed a project where it was
used to great effect) the fact that it doesn't support variable arrays (as
COBOL doesn't either) has no bearing on the use of collections or tuples.
Only when programmers get it into their heads that they can load a
collection into memory is there a requirement for an array. This is just old
thinking...manage the collection from wherever it is located! The whole
point of the collection is that its physical implementation is irrelevant.


>And yet given that ODOSLIDE
> directive in COBOL it is perfectly possible to create a collection with a
> variable number of elements and a variable number of value fields per
element,
> plus the elements can be n-dimensional..
>
No it isn't. It just seems that way <G>.

If you are determined to have the collection in memory you can get the same
result without ODOSLIDE. In either case you will have to allocate a maximum
occurrence. ODOSLIDE determines the location of
the item following the item that has OCCURS...DEPENDING ...ON in it, (but is
not subordinate to it). This is achieved by relocating the whole structure
at run time. It is an horrific overhead for a very little gain (a few bytes
of memory) but it does let you think that you have actually defined a
variable array... It isn't truly variable because what happened was that the
maximum size was allocated and then "adjusted" to suit. A Collection on the
other hand never  (well, it shouldn't...) allocates space (in any media)
that it doesn't need.

There is a difference between an unlimited number of elements and
"n-dimensional" also...

Pete.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-20T12:18:02-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a50p8s$ob5$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <E99c8.8683$ip2.1574102069@news.tli.de> <3c72d3d4_2@Usenet.com> <lxRc8.8748$te4.1583347780@news.tli.de>`

```
Markus,

There is a (fairly minor) difference between:

        01  TNUM PIC 9(18).
        01  FILLE1 REDEFINES TNUM.
            05 FILLE PIC 9 OCCURS 18.

and

    01  TNUM.
        05 FILLE  OCCURS 18 DEPENDING ON SUB5 PIC 9
           VALUE ZERO.
        05 FILL1 REDEFINES FILLE              PIC 9(18).

In your "new" coding TNUM is a numeric field and FILL1 is an alphanumeric
item.  In the original version, this was reversed.  If you need/want both an
alphanumeric and a numeric definition of the "whole" 18 characters, then you
should code it as:

  01  FILL1 PIC 9(18).
  01  TNUM REDEFINES FILL1.
        05  FILLE  OCCURS 18 DEPENDING ON SUB5 PIC 9
                          VALUE ZERO.


This should leave all the fields with the same attributes as the original
version of your code (and should compile cleanly)
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Redefinition of item containing an 'OCCURS DEPENDING ON' clause with MF 4.1

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-21T13:37:30+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c7442f2_7@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<Fdra8.8587$kd2.1540063346@news.tli.de> <E99c8.8683$ip2.1574102069@news.tli.de> <3c72d3d4_2@Usenet.com> <3C73F5A1.E3CAED55@ins-msi.com>`

```

Jeff Campbell <jcampbell@ins-msi.com> wrote in message
news:3C73F5A1.E3CAED55@ins-msi.com...
> I thought the ODO phrase was intended to make linear table searches more
> efficient.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> 8-)

That's a very good point you raised, Jeff.

It made me think and I came up with the following observations:

1. Linear table searches are usually on small tables. (otherwise we would
load the table sequentially and use a binary chop on it.) Personally, I use
SEARCH to do linear searches and SEARCH ALL to do binary chops.

2. There is a run time overhead in referencing items declared with ODO. This
overhead applies to every entry that is referenced and could therefore be
more than the "saving" that was expected by using ODO to "limit" the search
in the first place.

3. Modern processors, doing a linear search on a small to moderate size
table in memory will show very little gain if the search is limited by an
ODO. So our reason for doing it is really an aesthetic one (it makes us feel
good to know we have optimized something to the limit of
reasonability...<G>) This "limiting" of the search is based on the doubtful
proposition that what we are looking for is NOT there. If we KNOW that what
we are looking for IS there, then nothing at all is gained by limiting the
search. Similarly, if what we are looking for is there say, 90% of the time,
the overheads incurred in limiting the search  to accommodate 10% of the
access, may not be justified.

4. There is nothing to stop us from counting entries as they are loaded into
the table (or defining a table size variable if it is a static table defined
in WS). We can still use it to limit the search without the overhead of ODO.

some examples...

01   my-table.
       12 table-entries   pic x(30)
                               occurs 50
                               indexed by mt-x1.

01   my-table-last    pic s9(4) comp.

01   found-flag        pic x value space.
       88 foundit                 value '1'.
       88 not-found             value '0'.
......

*> the table has been loaded elsewhere and my-table-last was incremented
with
*> each entry. It now contains 23...
*>
      set mt-x1 to 1
      search table-entries
            at end
                    set not-found to TRUE
            when
                    mt-x1 > my-table-last
                    set not-found to TRUE
            when
                    table-entry (mt-x1) = thing-im-looking-for
                    set foundit to TRUE
      end-search
....

While this looks reasonably elegant at the source code level, and it
achieves the goal of NOT searching 27 unused entries in the table if what we
are looking for is not there, it also incurs an overhead... the table index
is checked on each iteration to see if it has reached the limit. With ODO
the WHEN clause that does this would not be necessary. However, with ODO,
every entry would need variable addressing with the concomitant register
loading and arithmetic for indirect addressing, so there is an overhead
there too. The point is that there are run time overheads that should be
balanced, whichever way you do it, IF you CARE about run time overheads!
(Since the invention of the Pentium Gig processor, I have stopped worrying
about it... let the sucker work; that's why it was invented..<G>)

These days I am much more concerned with readability and source elegance
than balancing marginal processor overheads.
(It is interesting how this emphasis has changed over years... in the 60s,
run time efficiency was EVERYTHING. That's why many people resisted COBOL as
it gained popularity. It could never reach the purism that Assembler could.
Bear in mind that many of the processes, procedures and practices which
today are taken for granted had not been formulated then... the last thing
on our minds was ease of maintenance. If you were a programmer you should be
able to understand program code without it being written with maintenance in
mind...By the late 70s, with the advent of serious transaction processing on
mainframes, we were still pretty obsessed with getting every bit of
performance, but it was tempered a bit by the knowledge that we might have
to come back to this code in a few years time so a few comments in it
wouldn't hurt...<G>. Today, I find that being able to maintain the code I
wrote years ago is pretty important. Nowadays I am packaging it as
components and eventually Web Services so, although the actual source code
is not important to other people, it is to me. The march of technology,
driven as always by demand in the Market Place, has brought us processors
where it really DOESN'T matter too much if something is not totally
optimized in source. None of us can tell whether a process takes 100
Nanoseconds or 110... (Please don't flood CLC with mail saying I am
advocating sloppy programming and it is OK to write crap code; I'm not. I'm
merely advocating a realistic balance based on what is available to us.)

For these reasons I shall continue to avoid ODO, but after reading your
post, Jeff, I MIGHT be inclined to limit serial searches, as shown above.

Pete.





 Posted Via Usenet.com Premium Usenet Newsgroup Services
----------------------------------------------------------
    ** SPEED ** RETENTION ** COMPLETION ** ANONYMITY **
----------------------------------------------------------        
                http://www.usenet.com
```

```
keith@homiski.com (Keith) wrote in message news:<5fcecd24.0202130741.7e88fd@posting.google.com>...
```

## Thread: OT - Humor (Operating Systems) — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT - Humor (Operating Systems)

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-13T16:22:03-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4eouh$3e0$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
If OS's were parties...

DOS: Everyone sits on hard chairs, with nothing to eat or drink, and talks.
No one laughs.

Windows: Lots of beer, but it's flat; lots of food, but it's cold; and the
fire alarm keeps going off so you have to go out and stand in the street,
then go back in.

Mac: A catered party where waiters take care of your every need, but if you
ask for unhealthy food they scold you and bring you a bran muffin.

Unix: There's no food or drink. But there's a great kitchen, and all the
equipment you need for brewing beer in the bathroom.

VMS: A gigantic banquet, but the keynote speaker is so boring that everyone
falls asleep and misses dinner.

MVS: A nineteenth-century dinner party - it lasts forever, has a million
rules, and you spend more time dressing for it than you do eating.

Amiga: Only two people come, and they sit together all night exclaiming
about how wonderful the food is.

NeXT: The invitations are so advanced that no one can find the party.

CP/M: Everyone sits on rocks and roasts bear meat they caught themselves
over the fire.
```

```
Linux: You set up the kitchen - and all works fine and reliable as long as

Until, however, the party comes to an end. Because the party was
running reliable for such a long time, nobody remembers how
to finish a party - was it "init something", or "shut up" or what?

So, for a decent shutdown, the host has to be shot.
```

## Thread: OT - Humor (some of my best friends are project leaders ...) — 3 msgs

### OT - Humor (some of my best friends are project leaders ...)

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-13T16:25:47-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4ep9t$p89$1@slb5.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Five cannibals get appointed as programmers in an IT company. During the
welcoming ceremony the boss says: "You're all part of our team now. You can
earn good money here, and you can go to the company canteen for something to
eat. So don't trouble the other employees".

The cannibals promise not to trouble the other employees.

Four weeks later the boss returns and says: "You're all working very hard,
and I'm very satisfied with all of you. One of our cleaners has disappeared,
however. Do any of you know what happened to her?" The cannibals disavow all
knowledge of the missing cleaner.

After the boss has left, the leader of the cannibals says to the others:
"Which of you idiots ate the cleaner?" One of the cannibals raises his hand
hesitantly, to which the leader of the cannibals says: "You FOOL! For four
weeks we've been eating team leaders, managers, and project managers and
no-one has noticed anything, and now YOU have to go and eat the cleaner!"
```

```
That depends on the Email "Program" you are using. You use the Object
Oriented Interface and the Email Program does the rest.
Microsoft Outlook provides a help file on the CD (not part of the standard
install) that explains (in Visual Basic terms) how to program the interface.
Essentially you make a call to create the object, and Set the attributes -
one of which is the addressee. I'm not sure exactly how you call to these
things in Net Express, but it's not any different than any other "API" Call.

Below are the instructions on how to load the help file...
The Visual Basic Help file for Microsoft Outlook is located in the ValuPack.
To install this Help file, do the following:

1 Quit Help.
2 Insert the Microsoft Office CD or the stand-alone Outlook CD.
3 In the ValuPack folder, double-click the MoreHelp folder.
4 Select the Vbaoutl.hlp and Vbaoutl.cnt files.
5 Copy these two  files to C:\Program Files\Microsoft Office\Office on your
hard drive.
6 When asked whether you want to replace the existing versions of these
files, click Yes.
7 To update the table of contents and the index so that they include the
topics in the files you just copied, point to Find on the Start menu, and
then click Files or Folders.

8 In the Named box, type *.gid.
9 In the Look in box, type C:\Program Files\Microsoft Office\Office, and
then click Find Now.
10 When the file names appear at the bottom of the dialog box, select all of
them and click Delete on the File menu.

Note   If you installed Office or Outlook from a corporate network, ask your
network administrator where the ValuPack files are located. If you installed
the application from 3.5-inch disks, the ValuPack isn't included. You can
find these files on the Microsoft Web site, however. To do this, point to
Microsoft on the Web on the Help menu, and then click Online Support.
```

- **From:** "D De Villiers" <~ddevilliers99@lando.co.za>

```
Mmm' CobolScript ? Does this mean you can include COBOL (eg. CobolScript)
inside HTML (like JavaScript) ?
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: CobolScript

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-23T09:46:01+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C7764D9.583E42FF@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<a8e585b.0202150546.303bfe24@posting.google.com> <a55ttj$hn5$1@ctb-nnrp1.saix.net>`

```
D De Villiers wrote:
> 
> Mmm' CobolScript ? Does this mean you can include COBOL (eg. CobolScript)
> inside HTML (like JavaScript) ?

No.

At least not with CobolScript.  Apparently you will be able to use
Fujitsu .NET Cobol (or whatever subset of Cobol it turns out to be) in
an ASP form but that is server side.

JavaScript is a client side script.  

CobolScript is a scripting language (ie interpreted) like Perl and
Python are, and can be used as a CGI script (as well as several other
things).  It is similar to Cobol, an average Cobol programmer should be
able to use it quickly without too many problems.  It is just that what
it does it does quite well, what it doesn't quite do can waste a lot of
time.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: CobolScript

- **From:** "D De Villiers" <~ddevilliers99@lando.co.za>


- **From:** "Acucorp News" <shaun_gough@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-19T13:37:20-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1451C740A890D411B65C00104B95B1C061A8FD@ras.acucorp.com>`
- **References:** `<2d1c2f2e.0202150715.b8ecbe2@posting.google.com> <qnab8.18895$n4.3270252@newsc.telia.net> <2d1c2f2e.0202160003.3e019868@posting.google.com>`

```
If the reports that you want to generate are from data within Vision files,
you can always use the AcuODBC product to load the data into any ODBC
compliant product, that allows the graphical reports to be generated with
data loaded.   For Example, Crystal Reports or Microsoft Excel / Access.

Otherwise ACUCOBOL-GT v5.2.0 has introduced graphical printing which allows
you to design the reports that you want to print.
```

### How to pass parameters to a COBOL program in CMS?

- **From:** mikey.unsafe@gmx.net (Mikey)
- **Date:** 2002-02-15T07:47:44-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<26282372.0202150747.26f8b4b3@posting.google.com>`


#### ↳ Re: How to pass parameters to a COBOL program in CMS?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-15T12:50:44-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4jli9$mnc$1@slb4.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<26282372.0202150747.26f8b4b3@posting.google.com>`

```
Assuming you mean a "user parameter" and not a "run-time parameter" AND
assuming you are using a currently supported COBOL compiler (under LE),
check out:

 CEE3PRM--Query Parameter String

at:

 http://publibz.boulder.ibm.com/cgi-bin/bookmgr_OS390/BOOKS/CEEA3031/3.5.12

If you are NOT running under LE, then there are some other options also
available.  Tell us what compiler (version and release) you are using.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: How to pass parameters to a COBOL program in CMS?

- **From:** mikey.unsafe@gmx.net (Mikey)


#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu Compiler Option

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <invalid@invalid.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-15T22:46:39+00:00

```
"TOM NJ9612" <tomnj9612@aol.com> wrote in message
news:20020215111348.10839.00002051@mb-ba.aol.com...

>
>      I have received the status 'JMP0310I'.  I know  what the
problem is.  I
> have checked for the status, but I get a COBOL error, Once I
acknowledge the
> error, I then recieve my error message. I would like to display my
error

>      I would like to know if thier is  a compiler option that will

> COBOL messages, and just display my messages.

There's a run-time option settable in the COBOL.CBR file.

Another way to attack it by using DECLARATIVES. Viz:

PROCEDURE DIVISION.
DECLARATIVES.
       DECLAR-INPUT SECTION.
           USE AFTER ERROR PROCEDURE ON INPUT CONTINUE.
       DECLAR-OUTPUT SECTION.
           USE AFTER ERROR PROCEDURE ON OUTPUT CONTINUE.
       DECLAR-IO SECTION.
           USE AFTER ERROR PROCEDURE ON I-O CONTINUE.
       DECLAR-EXTEND SECTION.
           USE AFTER ERROR PROCEDURE ON EXTEND CONTINUE.
       END DECLARATIVES.
PROCEDUR SECTION.  *>Deliberately misspelled.
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu Compiler Option

- **From:** pvieira@emporsoft.pt (Paulo Vieira)
- **Date:** 2002-02-15T16:11:57-08:00

- **References:** `<20020215111348.10839.00002051@mb-ba.aol.com>`

```
> 
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> Thanks in advance.

JMP030I is just a general error. The message you get must be much more
explicit. Using DECLARATIVES should just do what you want.
```

#### ↳ Re: MsCobol 4.5 and W2k

- **From:** Richard Plinston <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T12:08:28+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C70EEBC.FD8ECB5D@Azonic.co.nz>`
- **References:** `<xDab8.18897$n4.3271036@newsc.telia.net>`

```
Fim Wï¿½stberg wrote:
> 
> I have problem using MsCobol in W2k. When I try to
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> How to load ??

Windows NT, 2000 etc can execute OS/2 1.x programs in text mode (I don;t
think that XP still does though).  When you start MS Cobol 4.5 or MF
Cobol 3.x it tries to run as an OS/2 program and looks for those
components but fails because the appropriate OS/2 style environment
items are not set.

Use FORCEDOS to ensure that Cobol compiler and programs try to run as
DOS and thus find the run-time correctly.

Isn't this in the FAQ ?
```

<a id="t-406312b9ba"></a>
## Thread: Call an AST procedure from SYS$SETIMR in COBOL — 3 msgs

### Call an AST procedure from SYS$SETIMR in COBOL

- **From:** Dan_zero_count@yahoo.com (Dan Wilkes)
- **Date:** 2002-02-15T12:05:29-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<818e3959.0202151205.8271e35@posting.google.com>`

```
Does anyone please have an example of using SYS$SETIMR to initiate an
AST Procedure using COBOL, which they can share with me?

 I am clearly too dense to understand the manual regarding the AST
argument for a call to the system service $SETIMR. What are a
"procedure value" and "Call without stack unwinding" in COBOL?

<snip>....

  Open VMS Usage: AST_PROCEDURE
  Type          : Procedure Value
  Access        : Call without stack unwinding
  Mechanism     : 64-bit reference on Alpha, 32-bit on VAX


   Regards,

     Dan.
```

#### ↳ Re: Call an AST procedure from SYS$SETIMR in COBOL

- **From:** Jeff Campbell <jcampbell@ins-msi.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-17T07:30:30+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C6F52DF.C5828BE4@ins-msi.com>`
- **References:** `<818e3959.0202151205.8271e35@posting.google.com>`

```
Dan Wilkes wrote:
> 
> Does anyone please have an example of using SYS$SETIMR to initiate an
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
>      Dan.

Here's a quick hack, taken from example 8.1 in the "OpenVMS Programing
Concepts" manual. Example 8.1 is written in C. The trick is to let the
linker assign the address (procedure value) to the pointer variable.

See section 3.3 Procedure Representation in the "OpenVMS Calling
Standard"
manual.

--------

identification division.
program-id. x.

environment division.
data division.
working-storage section.
01  ast-proc-addr       pointer           value external ast_routine.

01  delta-time          pic s9(18)  comp  value -50000000.

01  return-value        pic s9(18)  comp.

* the SYS$SETIMR call returns these condition values:
    88    ss$_accvio                      value external ss$_accvio.
    88    ss$_exquota                     value external ss$_exquota.
    88    ss$_illefc                      value external ss$_illefc.
    88    ss$_insfmem                     value external ss$_insfmem.
    88    ss$_normal                      value external ss$_normal.
    88    ss$_unasefc                     value external ss$_unasefc.

procedure division.
call-set-timer-service.

    call "sys$setimr"
        using
            omitted
            by reference delta-time
            by value ast-proc-addr
            omitted
            omitted
        giving
            return-value
    end-call

    if ss$_normal
        display "sleeping for 5 seconds"

        call "sys$hiber"
            giving return-value

        end-call
                
    else
        evaluate true
            when ss$_accvio
                display "Expiration time not readable"

            when ss$_exquota
                display "Process AST or timer quota exceeded"

            when ss$_illefc
                display "Illegal event flag number specified"

            when ss$_insfmem
                display "Not enough dynamic memory to allocate timer
element"

            when ss$_unasefc
                display "Process does not have the specified event flag"

        end-evaluate

    end-if

    stop run

    .
                                                             
end program x.

identification division.
program-id. ast_routine.

environment division.
data division.
working-storage section.
01  return-value        pic s9(18)  comp.

procedure division.
ast-fired.

    call "sys$wake"
        using
            omitted
            omitted
        giving
            return-value
    end-call

    exit program

    .
                                                             
end program ast_routine.

-----

Jeff Campbell
n8wxs@arrl.net
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Call an AST procedure from SYS$SETIMR in COBOL

- **From:** Dan_zero_count@yahoo.com (Dan Wilkes)
- **Date:** 2002-02-19T12:05:30-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<818e3959.0202191205.120a9cc7@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<818e3959.0202151205.8271e35@posting.google.com> <3C6F52DF.C5828BE4@ins-msi.com>`

```
Thanks very much for the information Jeff, I have utilized it fully.
   Dan.

Jeff Campbell <jcampbell@ins-msi.com> wrote in message news:<3C6F52DF.C5828BE4@ins-msi.com>...
> Dan Wilkes wrote:
> > 
…[126 more quoted lines elided]…
> n8wxs@arrl.net
```

#### ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL v3 spacing

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <invalid@invalid.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-16T15:57:08+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ojvb8.53984$Aw2.3249725@bin7.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`
- **References:** `<9df21a1b.0202152252.26e6ae3c@posting.google.com>`

```

"Eric Anderson" <andersonem08@uww.edu> wrote in message
news:9df21a1b.0202152252.26e6ae3c@posting.google.com...
> I'm new to Cobol and have noticed that trying to double space a
report
> line doesn't work.  An example line:
>
> 01 DETAIL-LINE TYPE IS DETAIL LINE NUMBER IS PLUS 2.
>
> should double space, but no matter what number i use it always
single
> spaces.
>
> My instructor tells me that in this version of Fujitsu Cobol double
> spacing just isn't possible.  Anyone know a way to achieve this?

The LINE NUMBER clause is used for sending a line to the screen (or so
my manual says having, in several decades, never seen a program that
uses it). Are you, in fact, trying to send a report to the screen? The
reason I ask, it that 'double space' usually refers to a printout.

If the latter, use WRITE DETAIL-LINE AFTER 2.

If the former (screen), and again, never having known anyone who has
ever used this feature, a clue from my manual is that "... the LINE
NUMBER clause with PLUS cannot be specified as the first screen item."
Don't use DETAIL-LINE for the fist line of your report.

As an aside, you've demonstrated two principles. First, human
instruction is a swell supplement to a book. In a book, all the
commands are seemingly equally useful, all the print is the same size,
and it's up to the uninitiated to hook stuff together. An instructor
can emphasize or dismiss things based on his experience, thereby
simplifying the student's road to competence.

Second, and this is just my opinion, your instructor may have missed
his aforementioned duty by a) asserting Fujitsu doesn't support
'double spacing' (which I feel is EXTREMELY unlikely), and b)
Assigning a project with 'LINE NUMBER IS PLUS...' constructs.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Fujitsu COBOL v3 spacing

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>

```
OK - that is what I thought.

(Use of "report writer" is somewhat controversial in this newsgroup - but I
*like* it).

Now, my next question is whether you are look at a file or looking at the
output on a printer?  If it is going DIRECTLY to a printer, my guess is that
you WILL see double spacing.

If you send it to a file, then you will need to look at the file "in hex" to
see if there are line-feeds and/or carriage control characters in the file.
My *guess* is that there are such characters in the file, but they are not
showing up in the way you are "looking" at the print file.
```

<a id="t-8f64b8df58"></a>
## Thread: ACCESS 2000 dates in COBOL — 3 msgs

### ACCESS 2000 dates in COBOL

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T18:44:30+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c709798_1@Usenet.com>`

```
Has anyone found a way to get ACCESS 2000 to return a date as a 64 bit
floating point field (the way it is stored on the database)?

In ACCESS 97 you could define a field as DATE and use comp-2 in your COBOL
program to read and write it through ODBC. It recognised the standard VB
date format.

ACCESS 2000 returns a numeric character string that can never be matched to
a comp-2 field. It will WRITE a 64 bit comp-2 field correctly but it won't
read it back in the same format.

I believe there may be an option somewhere in the bowels of ACCESS 2000 that
will change this behaviour.

I can program round it, but it is clumsy and makes COBOL look stupid...<G>.

Any ideas?

Pete.

```

#### ↳ Re: ACCESS 2000 dates in COBOL

- **From:** "Lee Unterreiner" <flu@nospam.flu-ent.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-17T22:25:29-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4q6r6$86u$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3c709798_1@Usenet.com>`

```

"> I believe there may be an option somewhere in the bowels of ACCESS 2000
that
> will change this behaviour.
>

Pete,

The problem is not in Access.  It's the implementation of the ODBC driver.
There are some builtin functions in ODBC that set or return the various
pieces of the datetime field.  I don't recall the exact syntax, but a quick
search of MSDN will give you the answer(s).

Lee
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: ACCESS 2000 dates in COBOL

- **From:** "Peter E. C. Dashwood" <dashwood@nospam.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2002-02-19T02:11:51+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3c70fff1_3@Usenet.com>`
- **References:** `<3c709798_1@Usenet.com> <a4q6r6$86u$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Thanks Lee.

I already searched and found the functions that will do it, but it is
unwieldy and a pain.

No wonder people don't use DATE functions on ACCESS DBs...<G> (For most
stuff previously I have used CCYYMMDD and it works fine...the problem is
that you can't use such a field for date arithmetic in SQL)

For instance I could code under ACCESS 97:
...
       WHERE    (TCPIPAddress = :HV-TCPIPAddress) AND
                          (Timestampz = :HV-Timestampz)
...
Where "Timestampz" is defined on the database as type DATE and in the Host
Variables as type COMP-2.

Now (under ACCESS 2000) I have to code:

...
          WHERE (TCPIPAddress = :HV-TCPIPAddress) AND
                (DATEVALUE(Timestampz) = DATESERIAL(:getYEAR, :getMONTH,
:getDAY)) AND
                (TIMEVALUE(Timestampz) = TIMESERIAL(:getHOURS, :getMINS,
:getSECS))
...

I'm sure you're right and it is the new ODBC driver that simply doesn't
implement the VB Date format (64 bit float). But it DOES allow an insert
with this field set as comp-2! The problem arises when you need to access
the row and set search criteria (as above). If you have a comp-2 field in
the HV you get an error and no data returned. This is because it  actually
returns an 18 digit string and it won't convert this to floating point. So I
have to set an 18 digit number to receive this field, then break that down
into Year, Month, Day, Hour, Minute, and Second... good fun...

My advice to anyone looking at this would be to NOT design systems with DATE
type fields used as keys...

In fact I am seriously re-considering going back to CHAR (CCYYMMDD) and just
copping the hit on date arithmetic...

Pete.
```

- **From:** "Guenter Tschech" <Guenter.Tschech@nospam.newline-software.net>

```

Richard Plinston wrote:
> Lee Unterreiner wrote:
> >
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> basis to supplement their current revenue model.

.NET before everything else is a brand for "Microsoft in the new internet
age".
It applies to
* The Runtime (CLR), which indeed runs on multi-platform
* the .NET Servers, which are the well-known (both good and bad) MS server
products
* the Web Service architecture, which now is a standard served by IBM, SUN,
SAP and others (at least with words :)

You can of course work with .NET without using the internet at all; in my
eyes the great thing about it is
that you can write a COBOL program and deploy it using standard Internet
Browsers into your whole
company, so there is only ONE runtime for all programs, regardless of
language (as long as they support the CLR)
>
> > The single platform is Windows XP/2000/CE for now.  .NET applications
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>
This is true, but you can precompile your apps so no compiler will be
invoked when
the thing is copied to your device. This naturally limits the
platform-independence of
.NET, so you a re supposed to do this with care.
But .NET is designed with a JIT in mind, while java is not, so the java JIT
has a lot more
problems to solve than its .NET counterpart, so it's not a surprise that
.NET apps run
much faster than java compiled programs...
>
> > 3. Security to protect you from the outside world and vice versa.
>
> That has yet to be demonstrated.

It is demonstrated by the release of VisualStudio.NET, which is so secure
you cannot
even run your own app if it is run from a network share... (before you open
the security again)
the main problem here is that security is far too complex for the normal end
user
(and I's say even the normal programmer), so unsafe programs will arise
regardless of language...

>
> > 4. Seamless components. Gone are COM and ActiveX.
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>
When you follow MS, ActiveX is really! gone, for the CLR of .NET includes
features that
make ActiveX obsolete. With COM, it depends on your architecture. Using
plain .NET,
you don't need COM, either, but you'll find a lot of mixed environments (who
knows better
than COBOL programmers, that written code outlives any new technique...)

> > 6. The end of DLL hell.  The ONLY installer one needs is FTP or XCOPY.
>
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>
The .NET concept of "the end of DLL hell" is nothing new, it's just the
revival of
UNIX patterns that are known for a long time, so don't complain, the best
survives :-)

> > The end user platform is free.  Its builtin to XP and beyond.  Its
available
> > for 2000 and CE.  Yes, your favorite COBOL application running on a
> > hand-held or even a phone!
>
> The services that will link the end-users and servers, will however, not
> be free.

but again, .NET is not only about services, it's only the real NEW thing
that the
marketing people have understood (have you tried to explain technical
details of an
operating system to your marketing  staff ?)

> > The development environment does not run on 9x.
>
> I doubt that there is any technical reason for this, it is just that MS
> wants everyone to buy XP (see 'Revenue model').

There is technical reason for this: XP and NT is the same operating kernel
(XP is Windows NT 5.1),
whereas win98/winme sits on top of old DOS code.
But you can deploy .NET apps to Win98, and�be honest: would you like to
develop on a machine
where every program crashes the whole machine ?

- just my humble 2 cents (well, we do have cents in germany too, now :-)

Guenter <><
```

```
frequent comp.lang.cobol submitters).

where available
```

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### COBOL (et al) and z/OS.e

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T13:07:53-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4rjoo$ioh$1@slb3.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
FYI -

 at:
http://www-1.ibm.com/servers/eserver/zseries/library/specsheets/zos_zose/zos
e.html

"z/OS.e is specifically designed for today's popular applications such as
WebSphere�, Java, Enterprise Java (J2EE), C/C++ and Web-based data
transaction processing applications for a price performance that customers
expect. However, this offering will not support certain workloads such as
traditional CICS�, IMST, COBOL and FORTRAN."

at:

http://www-1.ibm.com/servers/eserver/zseries/library/specsheets/zos_zose/zos
e_specs.html

"Customers who  choose z/OS.e are not licensed to run the following
traditional  workloads on z/OS.e:

           a.. CICS

      a.. IMS

      a.. COBOL

      a.. Fortran

      However, precompiled COBOL DB2 stored procedures, and other
precompiled applications using the Language Environment preinitialization
interface (CEEPIPI) are supported. Customers may not use the following
compilers: COBOL, PL/I, VisualAge� PL/I, and FORTRAN. However, z/OS.e
supports execution of precompiled PL/I and VisualAge PL/I applications."




NOTE WELL:
  This information *only* applies to z/OS.e - and *not* to z/OS (V1R3)
itself.  COBOL (and PL/I and Fortran) compilers and applications - along
with CICS and IMS are "obviously" still supported there !!!
```

## Thread: "processor dependent" vs "optional" - a J4 paper — 10 msgs

_Topics: [`COBOL standards (ANS, ISO, 74/85/2002/2014)`](topics.md#standards)_

### "processor dependent" vs "optional" - a J4 paper

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T14:50:03-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a4rpe7$st3$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
I do NOT *personally* agree with the "conclusions" - but for those
interested in the (long lasting - but apparently resolved) issue of
"processor dependent" vs "obsolete" in the draft of the next COBOL Standard,
I would suggest you read the J4 paper at:

 http://people.ne.mediaone.net/doncobol/02-0052.doc

I have not (yet) seen/read the minutes of the meeting where this paper was
discussed, but it is my IMPRESSION that this paper DOES accurately reflect
the view of the MAJORITY (not unanimous) of members of J4 and WG4.
```

#### ↳ Re: "processor dependent" vs "optional" - a J4 paper

- **From:** stephenjspiro@mail.com (Stephen J Spiro)
- **Date:** 2002-02-18T22:35:37-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<928495c6.0202182235.15a3147d@posting.google.com>`
- **References:** `<a4rpe7$st3$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Bottom line is that they didn't want to make anything "officially"
optional (except the obsolete COMMUNICATION SECTION), so they made
"processor dependent" almost everything that anyone wanted to actually
be optional.  "Market positioning" has been defined as a
characteristic of the "processor".

In the real world, there is little here  that will have any
significant impact on programmers -- or even a mild impact on
programmers.

But it IS intellectually dishonest.  For the most part, this part of
the standard was hijacked by the compiler-makers, and at the end, some
people who might otherwise have opposed it did not want to delay the
standard any more.

Stephen J Spiro
Member, J4 COBOL Standards Committee
```

#### ↳ Re: "processor dependent" vs "optional" - a J4 paper

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-21T17:00:09-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a5456o$21qm$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<a4rpe7$st3$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`

```

"William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com> wrote in message
news:a4rpe7$st3$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net...

> I do NOT *personally* agree with the "conclusions" - but for those
> interested in the (long lasting - but apparently resolved) issue of
> "processor dependent" vs "obsolete" in the draft of the next COBOL
Standard,
> I would suggest you read the J4 paper at:
>
>  http://people.ne.mediaone.net/doncobol/02-0052.doc

From what I can gather, Bill, this is a "long lasting" issue only to those
who are opposed to the idea of "processor dependency" in the current draft.
The question has been brought up several times in my presence in J4
meetings, and each time the point is raised, it has been pointed out that J4
is producing this draft on behalf of ISO/IEC JTC1 SC22/WG4, that the
appropriateness and correctness of the term "processor dependent" in the
document they are asking J4 to develop has been repeatedly reaffirmed to J4,
and that the correctness of "market position" for a compiler as a
determining factor in processor dependency is likewise repeatedly
reaffirmed.

And the point is not ' "processor dependent" vs "obsolete" '.  There is only
one "optional element" in the Draft Standard:  the Communications Facility
and all the syntax associated with it.  There are, however, elements of the
syntax that are optional to the user -- for example, the ON SIZE ERROR
clause of the COMPUTE statement is optional (to the programmer, not to the
compiler).

The terminology controversy is between "processor dependent element" vs.
"optional element", and whether the same term should be used for both.  I
would argue that it should not.

Whether you call it "processor dependent element" or "blivet element" is not
particularly material to me personally, but at this stage in the development
of the Draft Standard, it is a little late in the game to change it to
something else, and to change the term to make it more ambiguous rather than
less does not strike me as an improvement.

Now, I understand the need for a conforming program compilable by one
vendor's conforming compiler without using any of that vendor's extensions
(which must in any event be flagged) to be compilable on any vendor's
conforming compiler.

Let's take USAGE BINARY as an example.  The current standard requires that
"a radix of 2 is used to represent a numeric item in the storage of the
computer."  in all conformant implementations.  The draft standard places
USAGE BINARY in the "processor dependent" category, because the authors felt
that it was not appropriate either to require that any hardware supporting
COBOL *must* support radix-2 arithmetic, or to require that the implementor
of a conformant compiler provide software simulation of such a feature!  I
would support a compiler implementor providing such a feature *if they
wished to do so*, but I am not at all convinced that a COBOL compiler on a
decimal machine would be worthless without USAGE BINARY!

There are other "processor dependent" features that are arguably more
divorced from the nuts-and-bolts of the Central Processing Unit on which the
program ultimately is to run, and that have been discussed over and over and
over again at both the US and the international standards body level.  I
think what's going to be "in" and what's going to be "out" of the draft
standard is pretty well set by international consensus at this point; we are
down to the final editing for typographical errors preparatory to submission
of the draft for an international ballot.

And, at this point, to pick some names relatively at random, I think the
formal opinion of the standards body of, say, the Netherlands or New Zealand
can reasonably be said to outrank the formal opinion of Bill Klein in this
matter.  J4 is responsible for the *development* of the standard, but
ISO/IEC JTC1/SC22/WG4 claims ultimate responsibility for its content, and I
believe they have spoken, loud and clear, on this issue, to J4.

The document you reference is a discussion defending the existence of
"processor dependent" (call them "blivet elements" if you prefer) in the
Draft Standard.  I strongly support the idea of a compiler implementor
providing all features that *can function* on the target machine *if they
wish to do so*.  I also believe the mandatory elements (like object
orientation and standard arithmetic) are appropriately mandatory for
conformant compilers even if some implementors find them onerous as
requirements.   But I do not believe the presence, or the contents, of this
two-page list represents a catastrophe for the standard.

>
> I have not (yet) seen/read the minutes of the meeting where this paper was
> discussed, but it is my IMPRESSION that this paper DOES accurately reflect
> the view of the MAJORITY (not unanimous) of members of J4 and WG4.

Discussions that do not have concrete outcomes are not typically recorded in
the J4 minutes.  The response in question has been discussed in at least two
meetings at which I was present.  The original text was made public in a
draft recommended response on April 19, 2001, in J4 document 01-0309, in
direct response to US public review comment #52 of the same date, reflected
in J4/01-0306.  This response was discussed at Meeting 230 in Roseville, CA,
at which you were present, and at which TWO straw votes were taken to
reaffirm the current definition of "processor dependency" in the FCD (the
straw vote count was seven in favor of that reaffirmation, one opposed).
The response discussed then has not changed much since then.

While you may not have read the minutes for that meeting, they have been
available on the web in draft form since last May and in final form since
last June.  The response, and its refinement, is reflected in several
editions of the tracking document for US responses since that meeting.  It
was made into a separate document in part because of the sheer length of the
comments that stimulated the response, and in part because a clear
explanation as to why J4 (and from all I can gather WG4) felt it unwise to
change the document in response to the comment required a lengthy answer.

You may not agree with, or even like J4's answer.  I think reflects not only
the consensus of J4 members over the last several meetings but also the
direction I believe J4 has received from the international standards body
for whom J4 is producing the document.   The Draft Standard will stand or
fall as an International Standard on the consensus of participating national
standards bodies in the upcoming months, and I believe J4 and the members
that participate in it have done their level best to provide a document that
will warrant that consensus.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

```
Grinder <grinder@no.spam.maam.com> wrote in message
```
