###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: High values in RM COBOL?

- **From:** "ronald leenheer" <r.leenheer@wanadoo.nl>
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T00:11:59+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<jvVe8.15$1V1.133@pollux.casema.net>`
- **References:** `<FaMe8.710$a%.24309@news.siol.net> <a5g4ol$e03$1@panix1.panix.com> <8a2d426e.0202261256.434a9bac@posting.google.com>`

```
Why not

03  AAA-X.
      05   AAA                     PIC 9(?)V9(?).
Don't redefine when its not needed. Use a grouplevel instead.
Keep your programs easy to read. Dont use AAA but a meaningful name.
Saves a lot of time when you have to maintain them 10yrs later.:)
I'm programming cobol now for 17yrs so I do not know of each program what it
does anymore.


"Jack Sleight" <jacksleight@hotmail.com> schreef in bericht

> > 2)  MOVE HIGH-VALUES TO WS-VARIABLES will populate AAA with
> > x'FFFFFFFFFF'... and everything else in WS-VARIABLES, as well; your
> > compiler will not, probably, allow the statement of IF AAA =
HIGH-VALUES.
> >
> > One can also REDEFINE the AAA field:
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> > problem with the compiler accepting IF AAA = HIGH-VALUES but a
work-around
> > would be:
> >
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> > DD
```

#### ↳ Re: High values in RM COBOL?

- **From:** "JerryMouse" <invalid@invalid.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-26T14:46:46+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<qdNe8.249655$eS3.17580522@bin3.nnrp.aus1.giganews.com>`

```
"Boris �avc" <boris.savc@odis-info.com> wrote in message
news:FaMe8.710$a%.24309@news.siol.net...
> 1. HIGH VALUES in RM COBOL only works for alfa-numeric fields and
not also
> for numeric like
> in AcuCobol (compiler itself sees if a field is numeric or alpha).
Is there
> some way to fix this or go around?
>
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> *****   1) 0653: W Sending nonnumeric literal value is not
compatible with
> receiving numeric or numeric edited data item.


You want to load a numeric data element with the maximum number that
will fit in the field?
```

#### ↳ Re: High values in RM COBOL?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-26T20:08:58-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a5hfea$vk2$1@slb3.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<FaMe8.710$a%.24309@news.siol.net>`

```
Others have responded and indicated that you need to have an alphanumeric
"variation" of the field to move high-values to.  However, if you really DO
want to get the highest (or lowest) algebraic value in a field, you might be
interested in the new

   HIGHEST-ALGEBRAIC
    and
   LOWEST-ALGEBRAIC

intrinsic functions that are introduced in the draft COBOL Standard.  If you
think these would be useful to your development environment, you might want
to contact Liant about their adding these features to their product
(when/before they add support for the full revision).
```

#### ↳ Re: High values in RM COBOL?

- **From:** "Tom Morrison" <t.morrison@liant.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T17:03:18+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<qj8f8.1583$Ch7.571836434@newssvr12.news.prodigy.com>`
- **References:** `<FaMe8.710$a%.24309@news.siol.net>`

```

"Boris �avc" <boris.savc@odis-info.com> wrote in message
news:FaMe8.710$a%.24309@news.siol.net...
> [snip] Is there some way to fix this or go around?

Others have suggested redefinition.  Actually, 1985 standard COBOL has a
mechanism to cast a numeric reference to alphanumeric: reference
modification.

Just change the code to:
MOVE HIGH-VALUE TO AAA(1:).

Tom Morrison
Liant Software Corporation
```

```
Your process is confused ("I am able to link it(*.COB) and it becomes
and .OBJ"):

Linkers don't read source files and linkers don't produce OBJ files.

Source(xxx.COB) -> {Compiler} -> xxx.OBJ -> {Linker} => xxx.EXE
```

## Thread: Squares in my output file??????????????? — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Help requests and how-to`](topics.md#help)_

### Squares in my output file???????????????

- **From:** jfrick@sc.rr.com
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T02:18:03+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<75go7ucq7k2ou9m447cgrv6dv3l2tbhqi0@4ax.com>`

```
I wrote a program and finally got it to run but my output file ended
up with squares throughout it in between my headings and data. Why did
this happen? 

Jim
jfrick@sc.rr.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Squares in my output file???????????????

- **From:** lsunley@mb.sympatico.ca
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T03:55:28+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ZpzG4UNLyRNq-pn2-3NxqulkTiUMl@thishost>`
- **References:** `<75go7ucq7k2ou9m447cgrv6dv3l2tbhqi0@4ax.com>`

```
On Wed, 27 Feb 2002 02:18:03 UTC, jfrick@sc.rr.com wrote:

> I wrote a program and finally got it to run but my output file ended
> up with squares throughout it in between my headings and data. Why did
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> 

A bug :-)

You did not initialize your working storage areas with spaces.
```

#### ↳ Re: Squares in my output file???????????????

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald_tees@sympatico.ca>
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T00:55:48-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Cv_e8.74591$JZ.9204335@news20.bellglobal.com>`
- **References:** `<75go7ucq7k2ou9m447cgrv6dv3l2tbhqi0@4ax.com>`

```
The fields are initialized to nulls instead of spaces.  You are probably
setting up the title as so:
01 title.
    02 filler        picture x(4) value "word".
    02 filler        picture xx.
    02 filler        picture xx value "cc
The filler between the words is not initialized (make it space with a value
statement).

Donald

<jfrick@sc.rr.com> wrote in message
news:75go7ucq7k2ou9m447cgrv6dv3l2tbhqi0@4ax.com...
> I wrote a program and finally got it to run but my output file ended
> up with squares throughout it in between my headings and data. Why did
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

#### ↳ Re: Squares in my output file???????????????

- **From:** "Michael Mattias" <michael.mattias@gte.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T13:01:12+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<sM4f8.4647$E11.783@nwrddc02.gnilink.net>`
- **References:** `<75go7ucq7k2ou9m447cgrv6dv3l2tbhqi0@4ax.com>`

```
<jfrick@sc.rr.com> wrote in message
news:75go7ucq7k2ou9m447cgrv6dv3l2tbhqi0@4ax.com...
> I wrote a program and finally got it to run but my output file ended
> up with squares throughout it in between my headings and data. Why did
> this happen?

If you are trying to read your output in Microsoft Word(r), carriage returns
also appear as "squares." (This also happens with WordPad, but not with
NotePad).

If you want to check your output completely, view it with a hex viewer,
looking for CR, LF or CRLF at the end of lines in addition to embedded NULs
(x'00').

You can solve embedded nulls easily enough using INSPECT
CONVERTING|REPLACING just prior to writing, although MOVE'ing SPACE to the
output group item, INITIALIZE'ing the print line record, then MOVE'ing the
data would be more elegant and is the recommended method.

When I am going to create a "report file" which goes to disk, I generally
make the file SEQUENTIAL rather then LINE SEQUENTIAL and explicitly write
the end-of-line terminator desired.

MCM
```

#### ↳ Re: 3270 data streams

- **From:** scolby1606@aol.com (SColby1606)
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T07:32:40+00:00

```
The book you want is the '3270 data stream programmers guide' (IBM). If you do
a search you should be able to find it online.

It's kind of heavy going and ranks up there with ESA/390 Principles of
Operation as a good book for insomniacs, but it does have everything you need
to know about writing, using, and debugging 3270 data streams.

Steve
```

```
The IBM Visualage COBOL 2.2 version is available for OS/2 (and it 
works fairly well). Microfocus used to have the Workbench 4.0 compiler
for OS/2 but getting it is harder than finding hen's teeth.
```

<a id="t-36e02170ca"></a>
## Thread: IBM Mainframe COBOL - What versions do you use? — 7 this month / 33 total

_Topics: [`Mainframe, z/OS, JCL, CICS`](topics.md#mainframe)_

### IBM Mainframe COBOL - What versions do you use?

- **From:** Colin Campbell <cmcampb@attglobal.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T15:04:02-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C7D65E2.91358189@attglobal.net>`

```
I'm part of a team studying the implications of our customers remaining
on OS/VS COBOL.  The study started from one CICS shop that read the CICS
TS V2.3 announcement, which essentially says you'll no longer have a
separate COBOL Translator for CICS at that release.  (The translator is
integrated into the IBM COBOL compiler, so you'd need to be using the
current compiler.)  This would allow OS/VS COBOL programs to run, but
would keep them from being changed.

DB2 V7 seems to say similar things; there will be an integrated
pre-compiler in COBOL for OS/390 & VM V2R2, although I don't know for
sure that the integrated pre-compiler for SQL will be the ONLY way to
pre-compile.

There doesn't seem to be any imminent deadline for executing load
modules compiled with OS/VS COBOL.  CICS made noises in this direction,
but have since withdrawn those statements, I believe.  The latest we've
been ale to get from IBM says that Language Environment will continue to
support OS/VS COBOL into the foreseeable future.  However, our customer
is running CICS with LE, but their batch is using the OS/VS COBOL run
time library.  IBM understandably won't say anything "supportive" about
that!

Some people we've talked to have said they had assumed the world had
already finished converting to "new COBOL", because they had done so.
Some IBM folks we've talked to have expressed surprise (maybe even
shock) that the customer hasn't really even begun to convert.  After
all, conversion could have begun as long as 18 years ago when VS COBOL
II was announced.

Since looking at the first shop, the customer has told us that at least
two more of their divisions are in similar shape.  (The first shop is
roughly 80% OS/VS COBOL, most of the rest is VS COBOL II, with a very
few COBOL for MVS & VM load modules.)  They are starting to look at this
as an enterprise wide problem.  The shop where I do most of my work is
only about 40 - 50% converted, though we're going at it pretty hard
now.  This shop supports another large customer, and I recently learned
that another application group has hardly begun to convert.  In fact, I
helped the programmer there get his first run unit to execute just last
week.

My company, an IT services provider, is starting to listen to those of
us who've been crying wolf.  They may tackle the issue as something they
MUST do for their customers, to keep their mainframe applications
viable.

I'm curious.  Those of you who can share the information, what does your
shop look like in terms of load modules compiled (and executing) with
OS/VS COBOL vs. VS COBOL II vs. "new COBOL" (COBOL/370, COBOL for MVS &
VM, COBOL for OS/390 & VM, etc.)?

Are you starting to worry about your exposure if you still have OS/VS
COBOL running?

Thanks for the information!
```

#### ↳ Re: IBM Mainframe COBOL - What versions do you use?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-27T17:44:52-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a5jr1o$7nm$1@nntp9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3C7D65E2.91358189@attglobal.net>`

```
Colin,
  Let me start by saying that I have heard *RUMORS* that run-time support
for OS/VS COBOL programs under CICS *might* be extended.  However, the most
recent OFFICIAL statement from IBM is at:
  http://www.ibmlink.ibm.com/usalets&parms=H_201-354

which explicitly says (for CICS TS V2R2 and for the "next" release after
that),

"Translator support for the earlier (pre-Language Environment) compilers
OS/VS COBOL (5740-CB1, 5740-LM1, and 5734-CB4), VS COBOL II (5668-958, also
5688-023), OS PL/I Version 1 (5734-PL1), OS PL/I Version 2 (5668-910, also
5668-909), and SAA� AD/Cycle� C/370T (5688-216) is withdrawn and is not
available in this release. It is planned that run-time support for OS/VS
COBOL programs (regardless of run-time library used) and for any other
programs running under pre-Language Environment run-time libraries will be
withdrawn from the next release."

NOTE WELL: the "integrated" CICS/compiler support *only* works for IBM COBOL
for OS/390 & VM V2R2 (via APAR) or IBM Enterprise COBOL for z/OS & OS/390
(built-in).  IBM has indicated that if you "save" off the translator from
earlier releases, that it probably work with newer releases of CICS - but
that does NOTHING for OS/VS COBOL programs running under CICS.

Remember that the latest version of COBOL (Enterprise COBOL) has dropped
support for CMPR2 (VS COBOL II, R2 and '74 Standard) support.  So I do
believe that IBM is QUITE serious about "dropping" support for older COBOL
compilers and interfaces.
```

#### ↳ Re: IBM Mainframe COBOL - What versions do you use?

- **From:** yukonmama@aol.com (YukonMama)
- **Date:** 2002-02-28T03:12:06+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<20020227221206.01741.00000680@mb-ft.aol.com>`
- **References:** `<3C7D65E2.91358189@attglobal.net>`

```
>From: Colin Campbell cmcampb@attglobal.net 
>Date: 2/27/02 6:04 PM Eastern

>'m curious.  Those of you who can share the information, what does your
>shop look like in terms of load modules compiled (and executing) with
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>Thanks for the information!

Back when Y2K loomed large over the horizon we were given the edict to convert
all our programs to VS COBOL II in an attempt to get everything AMODE (31). 
Some programs refused to convert (well - probably the programmer just didn't
feel like it) and we more or less now have everything at that level.  We now
have COBOL for OS/390 and as we pull programs for maintenance or write new ones
this is what they are compiled with - IF they aren't on the library with the
OS/VS Cobol type.  When we do find one with this type we are supposed to
upgrade it but again some people just don't bother.  We're running CICS 4.1 and
going to a TS version any time soon (read until forced to do so) means we
aren't in a panic that some of our CICS is still chugging away as OS/VS COBOL.,
which also translates that going to the next release of COBOL won't happen any
time soon (again - read forced to do so). 

When the time comes that we must upgrade I'm sure THAT's when management will
be concerned about what version of Cobol we're using.  Until then it's 'if it
ain't broke don't fix it'.  Then it will be 'why didn't you fix it sooner?'.
```

#### ↳ Re: IBM Mainframe COBOL - What versions do you use?

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@worldnet.att.net>
- **Date:** 2002-02-28T09:23:19+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3C7DF6DE.453B4F28@worldnet.att.net>`
- **References:** `<3C7D65E2.91358189@attglobal.net>`

```
Colin Campbell wrote:
> (snip)
> I'm curious.  Those of you who can share the information, what does your
> shop look like in terms of load modules compiled (and executing) with
> OS/VS COBOL vs. VS COBOL II vs. "new COBOL" (COBOL/370, COBOL for MVS &
> VM, COBOL for OS/390 & VM, etc.)?

My shop probably only has about 4000 COBOL programs in production. 
Very few of them are still in OS/VS COBOL.  Probably more than 50% of
our non-obsolete programs were last compiled with COBOL for MVS & VM
or COBOL for OS/390 & VM 2.2.0.  My guess is that less than 5% of our
non-obsolete programs were last compiled with OS/VS COBOL.  During our
Y2K runup we were requested to recompile all programs with COBOL II. 
Naturally, we missed a few, but it didn't cause us any problems then.

We replaced the OS/VS COBOL runtime library with the COBOL II runtime
library around 1990.  A few early adopters began writing COBOL II
programs around 1992, and we were very fortunate in that none of our
COBOL II programs ever had the "compatibility with Release 2" option. 
We converted to LE/MVS runtime in 1998, again for Y2K reasons.

We converted all of our CICS regions (about 90 of them) from CICS 4.1
to Transaction Server 1.3 last year.  We currently run OS/390 2.8 but
some test LPARS are already on 2.10.  We expect production LPARS to be
upgraded to 2.10 by mid-March at the latest.

Last year we had a big project to convert all COBOL programs to
AMODE(31),RMODE(ANY).  Naturally we missed a few.  Some could not be
converted because they called pre-XA assembler subprograms (usually
for tape access) that could not be changed for various reasons.  One
problem is the lack of skilled assembler programs in applications.

Another development group recently replaced a very large financial
application with a new version written entirely in LE-enabled COBOL. 
This application must run in an LPAR with ALL31(ON).  It turns out
they can't even test their programs in an LPAR with ALL31(OFF).  Our
sysprogs have been trying to convert other LPARS to ALL31(ON) and now
the problems are really biting us.

Of course, you could add an ALL31(OFF) parameter to the execute
statement, but that doesn't work for programs that have an assembler
main calling a COBOL subprogram.  We have a lot of work to do.  

> 
> Are you starting to worry about your exposure if you still have OS/VS
> COBOL running?
> 
> Thanks for the information!

If it's a batch OS/VS COBOL program, running as main, I wouldn't worry
too much.  You can always add ALL31(OFF) to the JCL.  

I don't believe we have any CICS programs still running that were last
compiled with OS/VS COBOL.  But then again, it's always possible to
miss one.
```

```
We currently have 434 batch COBOL II DL/I programs that, unfortunately,
have included the DLZBPJRA module in them.  These programs will not run
as-is under LE.  Starting 'any day now' our QC department will be
recompiling most of these programs (over 100 are one time onlys so

violations in our CICS regions.  IBM's answer is "use COBOL/VSE, LE and
CICS TS".  Will it really make a difference?  Who knows.  Personally,
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: IBM Mainframe COBOL - What versions do you use?

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-28T22:52:54-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a5n1fc$cu4$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<3C7D65E2.91358189@attglobal.net> <3C7EF9E9.A55EAA7D@sprynet.com>`

```
Frank,
  Are you considering moving from the VS COBOL II or the DOS/VS COBOL
run-time to the LE run-time for your CICS regions?  Both of them are
"non-trivial" - but the move from the DOS/VS COBOL run-time is certainly
MORE difficult.

I know the MVS (OS/390, z/OS) environment much better than VSE, but you will
want to check out the RECOMMENDED run-time options for LE very carefully.
The "provided" defaults are AWFUL and IBM knows/knew it.  On the OS/390
side, they have "corrected" the defaults, but as I recall LE/VSE is *quite*
down-level compared to LE for OS/390 & z/OS.

If you have already moved to the VS COBOL II run-time, I am certain that you
have discovered "WSCLEAR" for CICS regions.  Well, in LE - it goes away -
and you need to set your STORAGE run-time option to "clear" storage.
ABEND/TRAP handling is also a BIG deal when moving to LE.  If you set your
run-time options correctly, then things shouldn't be "too bad" - but they
are still noticeable.  (Are you using Intertest? Xpediter? or some other
"interactive" debugging tool?  If so, check that you are on the correct
release to use LE - and how to set up your LE environment for them.)

As always, DO check out both the COBOL and the  LE "Migration Guides".  They
really can save a lot of pain in such conversions.
```

```
Hallo,

ich habe zwar meine Problem mit dem Display-Befehl schon in englisch in dies
Newsgroup gestellt, aber Ich m�chte es trotzdem noch mal in deutsch
versuchen ( und hoffe, da� ich so die Antworten besser verstehe ).

Das Programm :

Zentrum des Programmes ist ein 102400 Byte gr��ers Array, in das diverse
Informationen abgespeichert werden. Beim Auslesen des Puffers hatte ich
einige Probleme, soda� ich die betreffenden Section�s mit sehr vielen
Display-Befehlen ausgestattet habe. Bei der Ablaufkontrolle des Programmes
bin ich dann auf folgende Zeilen gesto�en :

DURCHLAUF NR. 000001814 SHOWZEIGER : 0047899
DURCHLAUF NR. 000001815 SHOWZEIGER : 0047946
DURCHLAUF NR. 000001816 SHOWZEIGER : 0047974
DURCHLAUF NR. 000001817 SHOWZEIGER : 0047992

Zubeachten ist die vorletzte Zeile **** VIM. Das ***** VIM START
*****-Display wurden von folgender Section erzeugt :

U99-DISPLAY SECTION.
    DISPLAY '***** VIM START *****'
    DISPLAY 'LOW-ZEIGER  : ', W1AN-SHEAD-LZEIGER
    DISPLAY 'HIGH-ZEIGER : ', W1AN-SHEAD-HZEIGER
    DISPLAY 'SHOW-ZEIGER : ', W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
    DISPLAY 'TEMP-ZEIGER : ', W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
    DISPLAY 'KILL-ZEIGER : ', W1AN-SHEAD-KZEIGER
    DISPLAY 'LOOP-ZEIGER : ', W1AN-SHEAD-LOOP
    DISPLAY ' '
    DISPLAY 'TRANSFER MENGE  : ', W1AN-STRANS-MENGE
    DISPLAY 'TRANSFER STRING : ',
             W1AX-STRANS-STRING(1:W1AN-STRANS-MENGE)
    DISPLAY 'PREFIX-LAENGE   : ', W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE
    DISPLAY 'PREFIX-STRING   : ',
             W1AX-PREFIX-STRING(1:W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE)
    DISPLAY ' '
    DISPLAY 'PREFIXVERGLEICH : '
    DISPLAY 'TRANSFER STRING : ',
             W1AX-STRANS-STRING(1:W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE)
    DISPLAY 'PREFIX-STRING   : ',
             W1AX-PREFIX-STRING(1:W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE)
    DISPLAY 'AKTUELLER RETURNCODE : ', W1AN-SHEAD-RCODE
    DISPLAY '***** VIM ENDE *****'
    DISPLAY ' '
    .

Wie zu sehen ist werden alle Display�s wie gew�nscht ausgef�hrt, und das
letzte Display, das mit eiem Inhalt versehen ist, wird teilweise wiederholt.
Es wird als erstes Zeichen eine Space ausgegeben, dann folgen 8 Zeichen aus
dem letzten Display mit Inhalt.

Der Fehler tritt an einer fest vorhersagbaren Stelle auf, und betrifft immer
das letzte Display vor folgender Markierung "<- Fehler" in der Section
U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING. W�rde ich aus dem Programm alle Diplay l�schen, und an
die "<- Fehler"-Stelle das DISPLAY "1234567890123" stellen, w�rde die
Ausgabe so aussehen ->
1234567890123
 23456789
1234567890123

Der Fehler wirkt sich nur einmal in dem Programmablauf aus, und tritt immer
auf wenn die Section�s U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING/U99-SHOW-NEXT im N�CHSTEN
Durchlauf in dem Puffer einen zutreffenden String finden. In diesem Fall
wird eine String gesucht der mit "DRU" anf�ngt. Speicherauszug des Puffers
( in logischen Zeilen dargestellt ):

026PGM089100      DISPLAY ' '
016PGM089200      .
136DRU*********************************************************************.
..
052DRU021100 S B11-VORLAUF                        *
052DRU022600 S B21-EINGABE                        *

Ich habe diese Tabelle von Hand nachgebaut. Bitte entschuldigt kleine
Ungenauigkeiten. Die ersten drei Zeichen sind die reale L�nge des n�chsten
Datanelementes im Puffer. Bis zur Datenelement "026PGM089100      DISPLAY '
'" l�uft alles fehlerfrei. Die Zeile "016PGM089200      ." wird auch richtig
verarbeitet, nur wird das letzte Display, da� mehr als kein Zeichen ausgibt
nach oben genannter Regel wiederholt.

Das, was mich besonders verwundert hat, ist da� die Stell an der der Fehler
auftritt zwar vorhersagbar ist, aber die Grundlage der Vorhersage nicht die
Grundlage des Fehlers seien kann. Der Fehler tritt auf, wenn im n�chsten
Suchlauf im Puffer ein zutreffendes Datenelement gefunden wird, aber der
n�chste Durchlauf kann einfach nicht vor seiner T�tigkeit an einem Fehler
schuld sein. Andersherrum -> Der fehler tritt auf, wenn das letzte nicht
zutreffende Datenelement gefunden wurde. Aber wie kann das DISPLAY '*****
VIM ENDE *****' und DISPLAY ' ' ausgegeben werden um dann nochmal ein " ****
VIM" auszugeben. Die Zeile DISPLAY ' ' ist scheindbar dabei v�llig egal .

Zusammenfassung :

1. Der Fehler betrifft immer das letzte Display�s eines Strings, da� nicht
nur aus SPASES besteht, da� vor dem R�cksprung aus der Section
U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING ausgef�hrt wird, wenn im n�chsten Suchlauf ein
zutreffender String gefunden seien wird.
2. Dabei ist egal ob das DISPLAY aus U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING stammt oder z.B.
aus U99-DISPLAY kommt.
3. Das fehlerhafte DISPLAY beginnt immer mit einem SPACE (X'40') gefolgt von
8 Zeichen, als Wiederholung des Display�s nach Regel 1 und 2, und wird dann
abgeschnitten.
3. Die restliche Verarbeitung scheind von dem Fehler unber�hrt zu bleiben.
4. Schreibe ich den Output auf Platte ( siehe write in U99-SHOW-NEXT )
entsteht bei der Fehlerstelle eine Leerzeile.
5. Der Fehler wird nicht durch die Anzahl der zuverarbeitenen Datenelemente
beeinflu�t.
6. Der Output des Programmes ist i.O.
7. Es ist egal ob ein fester STRING oder eine Variable ausgegeben wird.
8. Das Progamm l�uft in einer MVS/TSO-Umgebung
9. Es wird kein Unterprogramm angesprochen
10. Das Programm ist ein Hauptprogramm
11. Es wird nicht DB2 oder CICS genutzt.

12. Bisher haben sich in meinem Arbeitsumfeld 8 Mitarbeiter, mit ca. 120
Jahren EDV-Erfahrung, an dem Fehler versuch, und sind gescheitert.
13. Ich ( 13 Jahre Programmiererfahrung ) versuche seid ca. 4 Monaten den
Fehler einzukreisen, und habe noch nicht mal den Ansatz einer Probelml�sung.
14. Folgende Section�s verarbeiten den Puffer ->
U99-KILL-SHOW-THING
l�scht das aktuelle Datenelement und defragmentiert den Puffer-speicher
U99-STEUER-BYTE-LEER
�berpr�ft ob Datenelement vorhanden sind
U99-GET-MCB
hohlt die L�nge des n�chsten Datenelementes
 U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING
zeigt das n�chste Datenelement zusammen mit U99-SHOW-NEXT
U99-SHOW-NEXT
zeigt das n�chste Datenelement zusammen mit U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING
U99-SHOW
zeigt das aktuelle Datenelement zusammen mit U99-SHOW-THING
U99-SHOW-THING
zeigt das aktuelle Datenelement zusammen mit U99-SHOW
U99-W1-STEUER-ENDE
ende-verarbeitung
U99-W1-STEUER-INIT
grundeinstellungen des Puffers
U99-RESTORE-STRANS-MENGE
ermittelt die L�nge des �bergebenen STRINGS und schneidet den alles nach dem
letzten Buchstaben einer Zeile ab. Dieses Section arbeitet nur mit
TEXT-STRINGS
 U99-TEST-FREE-MEM
�berpr�ft den freien Speicher im Puffer
 U99-PUSH
sichert den aktuell �bergebenen String in den Puffer zusammen mit
U99-PUSH-DATA-STRING
U99-PUSH-DATA-STRING
sichert den aktuell �bergebenen String in den Puffer zusammen mit U99-PUSH
U99-BAUE-MCB
legt die L�nge des Datenelementes ab.
U99-DISPLAY
Display aller wichtigen Variablen des Puffers

2*************************************************************************
U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING SECTION.
PERFORM U99-STEUER-BYTE-LEER
IF W1AN-SHEAD-RCODE = 0
 PERFORM U99-GET-MCB
COMPUTE W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER           = W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
                                                                          +
W1AN-STRANS-MENGE

 IF W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER > W1AN-SHEAD-GROESSE (
 COMPUTE W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER          = W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
                                                                         -
W1AN-SHEAD-GROESSE
END-IF

MOVE 1                              TO W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
PERFORM W1AN-STRANS-MENGE TIMES
 MOVE W1AX-STEUER-BYTE(W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER)
 TO W1AX-STRANS-STRING(W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER:1)
 ADD 1                              TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
ADD 1                              TO W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
IF W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER > W1AN-SHEAD-GROESSE
MOVE 1                            TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
END-IF

END-PERFORM

 IF W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-HZEIGER
 MOVE W1AN-SHEAD-LZEIGER            TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
MOVE 'J'                           TO W1A8-LOOP
 END-IF
ELSE
 MOVE 0                              TO W1AN-STRANS-MENGE
 MOVE 'BYTE-PUFFER LEER!'            TO W1AX-STRANS-STRING
END-IF
<- Fehler
!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!
!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!
 .


3****************************************************************
U99-SHOW-NEXT SECTION.

 IF W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE > 0

 PERFORM WITH TEST AFTER
 UNTIL (
 W1AX-STRANS-STRING(1:W1AN-STRANS-MENGE)
 = W1AX-STRANS-STEMP(1:W1AN-STRANS-MTEMP)
 AND (W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-LOOP
           OR W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-LOOP
                                      + W1AN-STRANS-MENGE))
            OR W1AX-STRANS-STRING(1:W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE)
             = W1AX-PREFIX-STRING(1:W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE)

ADD 1 TO DUMMDUMM
 MOVE SPACES TO AB1AX-ZEILE
STRING 'DURCHLAUF NR. '               DELIMITED BY SIZE
DUMMDUMM                      DELIMITED BY SIZE
 ' SHOW-ZEIGER : '             DELIMITED BY SIZE
 W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER            DELIMITED BY SIZE
INTO AB1AX-ZEILE
 WRITE AB1-PROGA
DISPLAY 'DURCHLAUF NR. ', DUMMDUMM, ' SHOWZEIGER : ',
 W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER

PERFORM U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING
 END-PERFORM

IF W1A8-PREFIX-NONSHOW
 MOVE 1                            TO W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
 COMPUTE W1AN-SHEAD-KZEIGER          = 1
                                      + W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE

 PERFORM WITH TEST AFTER UNTIL W1AN-SHEAD-KZEIGER
                                 > LENGTH OF W1AX-STRANS-STRING
MOVE W1AX-STRANS-STRING(W1AN-SHEAD-KZEIGER:1)
TO W1AX-STRANS-STRING(W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER:1)
 ADD 1                             TO W1AN-SHEAD-TZEIGER
ADD 1                             TO W1AN-SHEAD-KZEIGER
END-PERFORM

COMPUTE W1AN-STRANS-MENGE           = W1AN-STRANS-MENGE
                                      - W1AN-PREFIX-LAENGE
END-IF

ELSE
PERFORM U99-SHOW-NEXT-THING
END-IF

IF   W1AX-STRANS-STRING(1:W1AN-STRANS-MENGE)
= W1AX-STRANS-STEMP(1:W1AN-STRANS-MTEMP)
AND (W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-LOOP
           OR W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-LOOP
                             + W1AN-STRANS-MENGE )
MOVE 2                             TO W1AN-SHEAD-RCODE
MOVE SPACES                        TO W1AX-STRANS-STRING
MOVE 0                             TO W1AN-STRANS-MENGE
END-IF

IF W1A8-LAST-OTHER
 MOVE 'N'                           TO W1A8-LAST-ACTION
MOVE W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER            TO W1AN-SHEAD-LOOP
 MOVE W1AX-STRANS-STRING(1:W1AN-STRANS-MENGE) TO W1AX-STRANS-STEMP
MOVE W1AN-STRANS-MENGE             TO W1AN-STRANS-MTEMP
 END-IF
 .

4***************************************************************************
**********
U99-STEUER-BYTE-LEER SECTION.
    IF W1AN-SHEAD-LZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-HZEIGER
     ADD 1                               TO W1AN-SHEAD-RC4
     MOVE 4                              TO W1AN-SHEAD-RCODE
    ELSE
     ADD 1                               TO W1AN-SHEAD-RC0
     MOVE 0                              TO W1AN-SHEAD-RCODE
    END-IF
    .
5*********************************************************************

U99-GET-MCB SECTION.
     IF W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER = W1AN-SHEAD-HZEIGER
      MOVE W1AN-SHEAD-LZEIGER            TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     END-IF
     MOVE W1AX-STEUER-BYTE(W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER)
                                         TO W1AX-STRANS-MENGE1
     ADD 1                               TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     IF W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER > W1AN-SHEAD-GROESSE
      MOVE 1                             TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     END-IF
     MOVE W1AX-STEUER-BYTE(W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER)
                                         TO W1AX-STRANS-MENGE2
     ADD 1                               TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     IF W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER > W1AN-SHEAD-GROESSE
      MOVE 1                             TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     END-IF
     MOVE W1AX-STEUER-BYTE(W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER)
                                         TO W1AX-STRANS-MENGE3
     ADD 1                               TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     IF W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER > W1AN-SHEAD-GROESSE
      MOVE 1                             TO W1AN-SHEAD-SZEIGER
     END-IF
     .

N�chstes zuverarbeitendes Byte : 116
LOW-ZEIGER                      -> erstes Byte, das benutzt wird ( ist immer
nach erfolgreicher Verarbeitung 1 )
HIGH-ZEIGER : 0052315     -> letztes benutztes Byte im Puffer
SHOW-ZEIGER : 0047992   -> das n�chste Byte was verarbeitet wird
TEMP-ZEIGER : 000000016 -> ist z.Z. egal, da er nur zum Puffern von andern
Zeigern oder kurzfristig genutzt wird
KILL-ZEIGER : 0000000       -> wird nur zum L�schen von Datenelemente und
zur folgender Defragmentierung des Speichers genutzt
LOOP-ZEIGER : 000048035 -> wird nur zum Sichern der Stratposition vor einem
Suchvorgang genutzt

TRANSFER MENGE  : 015                        -> Byteanzahl des aktuellen
Strings
TRANSFER STRING : PGM089200     .    -> das Datenelement, das gesichert
werden soll oder gesucht wurde
PREFIX-LAENGE   : 003                            -> Anzahl der gew�nschten
Prefix-Stellen
PREFIX-STRING   : DRU                           -> Der Prefix der, wenn
gew�nscht, vor das Datenelement gestellt wird.

TRANSFER STRING : PGM     -> Das im Puffer gefundene Element
PREFIX-STRING   : DRU          -> Der gesuche Prefix
AKTUELLER RETURNCODE : 00  -> Der h�hste Returncode, der bis zu diesem
Zeitpunkt entstanden ist.

Info: Beim vorletzten Suchlauf steht der SHOWZEIGER au�erhalb des aktuell
genutzten Speicherbereiches. Vor der n�chsten Suchaktion wird der
SHOW-ZEIGER mit dem HIGH-ZEIGER verglichen. Ist der SHOW-ZEIGER gr��er als
der HIGH-ZEIGER wird der Wert aus dem LOW-ZEIGER in den SHOW-ZEIGER
�bertragen. Wie aus dem Joboutput zu erkennen ist springt der Puffer von
BYTE 52176 im Durchlauf 1848 auf das Byte 1 im Durchlauf Nr. 1849 und
erkennt, da� der Speicher einmal komplett durchsucht worden ist.
In dem *** INFOBLOCK VOM BYTE-PUFFER *** werden alle Returncode der
Verarbeitung zur�ckgegeben. Die Anzahl von 3665 fehlerfreien Zugriffen auf
den Puffer erkl�rt sich aus dem Aufbau des Datenbestandes im Puffer + suchen
der Zeile "PROCEDURE DIVISION                USING L1-PARM." + suchen aller
Elemente die den Prefix "DRU" haben.

Zum Schlu� kann ich nur nochmal wieder holen, da� nach meiner Meinung der
Fehler nicht in dem Programm zu finden ist. Meine Vermutung ist, da� es ein
Spooler gibt, in dem TSO/MVS oder das COBOL-PGM die Output�s ablegt und
irgendwas, was ich durch Zufall programmiert habe, diese Kommunikation
Spooler - XXXX st�rt.
```

## Thread: Excel Sort method — 1 this month / 8 total

_Topics: [`Object-oriented COBOL`](topics.md#oo) · [`VSAM, files, sorting`](topics.md#files)_

### Excel Sort method

- **From:** cseidel@ftlife.com (Chet)
- **Date:** 2002-02-28T13:45:26-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a41dabc6.0202281345.50e03da3@posting.google.com>`

```
I am looking for some advice from anyone who has successfully executed
the Excel sort method from COBOL (MicroFocus NetExpress 3.1 flavor). 
I have been struggling with this one for too long and I can't seem to
get the results I need.

What I am trying to do is apply a two column sort to a selected range.
 I started with a recorded macro from Excel to get the approximate
syntax.  Then I set about creating the range objects in my COBOL
program (no problem), setting the appropriate flags to pass to the
sort method, etc.  But I just can't get it to work.

Here's what I have:
 
05 Key1Range            object reference. *> Key ranges for Sort
Method
05 Key2Range            object reference.
05 Order1               usage XLSortOrder. 
05 Order2               usage XLSortOrder.
05 SortHeader           usage Xlyesnoguess.
05 SortOrientation      usage xlSortOrientation.

.....

initialize rangestring                     
move "B2" to rangestring.
invoke ExcelObject "getRange"
       using by reference rangestring
       returning Key1Range.
initialize rangestring.
move "A2" to rangestring.
invoke ExcelObject "getRange"
       using by reference rangestring
       returning Key2Range.
set xlDescending  of Order1     to true.
set xlDescending  of Order2     to true. 
set xlGuess       of SortHeader to true. 
set xlSortRows    of SortOrientation to true.
.....
initialize rangestring
move "A:F" to rangestring
invoke ExcelObject "getRange"
       using by reference rangestring
       returning ColumnsRange.
.....

This works:

invoke ColumnsRange "Sort"
       using Key1Range.

Sort order takes default of Ascending.

This works:

invoke ColumnsRange "Sort"
       using Key1Range
             Key2Range.

Also works:

invoke ColumnsRange "Sort"
       using Key1Range
             by value Order1.

This works, too:

invoke ColumnsRange "Sort"
       using Key1Range
             by value SortHeader.

Try putting this all together and things start getting weird.  First,
this one will execute without an exception but the sort orders are
ignored:

invoke ColumnsRange "Sort"
       using Key1Range
             by Value Order1
             Key2Range
             by Value Order2.

Maybe I need to use the olesup class method "setNamedParameters"? 
Same results.  Then add in the "Header" named parameter and it throws
an exception.

I am starting to lose track of what works and what doesn't and in what
combinations.  Any advice on how to proceed would be greatly
appreciated.

- Chet Seidel
Farmers and Traders Life Insurance Company
```

<a id="t-28addf62e1"></a>
## Thread: Generating Random Numbers — 1 this month / 7 total

_Thread started [2002-03](2002-03.md#t-28addf62e1)._

#### ↳ Re: Generating Random Numbers

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2002-02-28T22:42:17-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a5n0rf$gec$1@slb1.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<a5mpjn$jrf$1@news7.svr.pol.co.uk>`

```
Check out the intrinsic function RANDOM - it is probably best if you use the
date/time as a "seed value" -as the ANSI/ISO definition of FUNCTION RANDOM
is "pseudo-random" which means that given the SAME seed value, you get the
same series of returned values.
```

---
